<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mental-health">MENTAL HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>According to the World Health Organization (WHO), mental health is a state of emotional well-being which enables one to function comfortably within society and to be satisfied with one’s own achievements.</li>
<li>This is a state of balance between an individual and the surrounding world, a state of harmony between oneself and others, a co-existence between the realities of the self and that of other people and the environment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-mentally-healthy-person">Characteristics of a mentally healthy person<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-mentally-healthy-person" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>He has ability to make adjustments.</li>
<li>He has a sense of personal worth, feels worthwhile and important.</li>
<li>He solves his problems largely by his own effort and makes his own decisions.</li>
<li>He has a sense of personal security and feels secure in a group, shows understanding of other people’s problems and motives.</li>
<li>He has a sense of responsibility.</li>
<li>He can give and accept love.</li>
<li>He lives in a world of reality rather than fantasy.</li>
<li>He shows emotional maturity in his behaviour, and develops a capacity to tolerate frustration and disappointments in his daily activities.</li>
<li>He has a variety of interests and generally lives a well-balanced life of work, rest and recreation.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychiatry">Psychiatry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychiatry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is an art as well as medical science concerned with mental process of an individual, the interaction between the doctor, the patients and their relatives and workmates, in the process of identifying the problem and carrying out appropriate action.</li>
<li>Psychiatry generalized approach stresses the unity of the body and mind.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cfd50ff6">What do you understand by the term ‘mental illness’?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cfd50ff6" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is maladjustment in living. It produces disharmony in the person’s ability to meet human needs comfortably or effectively and function within a culture. An individual loses his ability to respond according to the expectations he has for himself and the demands the society has for him.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-mental-illness">Characteristics of mental illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Changes in ones thinking, memory, perception, feeling and judgement resulting in changes in talk and behaviour which appears to be deviant from previous personality or from the norms of the community.</li>
<li>These changes in behaviour causes distress and suffering to the individual or others or both.</li>
<li>Changes and the consequent distress cause disturbance in day-to-day activities, work and relationship with important others. (social and vocational dysfunction)</li>
</ul>
<p>Psychology: Science of behavior.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="historical-trends-in-psychiatric-nursing">Historical Trends in Psychiatric Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#historical-trends-in-psychiatric-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Psychiatric nursing, and the understanding of mental illness, with which it associates, has developed in several epochs through the centuries. You will now look at each of those epochs in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="demonological-period">Demonological Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#demonological-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>1 | Page</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The earliest records of a person believed to have suffered from mental illness relate to king Nebuchadnezzar, who ate grass believing that he was an ox. Another example is Ajax, who impaled himself on a sword believing that he was tormented by demons.</p>
<p>During that time people believed that the cause of mental illness was demons. The treatment was quite harsh, degrading and dehumanizing and involved beating, chaining, locking the individual up in a dark room and throwing the individual into rivers and ponds.</p>
<p>Those patients who escaped this harsh treatment survived on stealing food or eating wild fruits. Wild animals ate up those who inadvertently wandered into the forest.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="political-period">Political Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#political-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This period is associated with King Edward II of England.</p>
<p>During that time, a law was passed in the parliament to protect the property of the mentally sick. In the year 1403, the Sisters of the Order of Saint Mary managed to start a facility to care for the mentally sick at Bedlam. The facility was able to accommodate six patients only. Thereafter, other hospitals followed the example.</p>
<p>The cause of mental illness, however, was still thought to be demons. The treatment, therefore, remained more or less as in the demonological period. Facilities were often dark, humid and infested with lice. They were also overcrowded, leading to mass deaths during outbreaks of disease such as the plague.</p>
<p>In the early 18th century, the first qualified nurse was appointed to look after the mentally ill by Edward Tyson. However, although qualified, the nurses appointed to look after the mentally sick were equally harsh to patients.</p>
<p>Men and women were housed together and members of the public used to visit these facilities as a form of entertainment. It was at</p>
<p>St. Luke's hospital in London where this form of entertainment was eventually banned. In order to enforce the policy, members of the public were only allowed to see the mentally ill in the presence of an attendant after being issued with a ticket.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="humanitarian-period">Humanitarian Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#humanitarian-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During this period, reforms of the patient care system for the mentally ill began in France, followed by Britain and later America.</p>
<p>Reform in France started in 1793 at Bicetre Hospital in Paris.</p>
<p>Dr. Philippe Pinel unchained a group of patients who had been in chains for 30 years. He advocated kindness for mentally sick persons, and as a result there was a marked improvement in mentally sick patients.</p>
<p>William Tuke started reforms in Britain in 1796. He advocated humane treatment of the mentally sick. In addition, he introduced what we today call 'occupational therapy'. Men were involved in gardening while women were involved in sewing. Both men and women assisted attendants in their daily work activities. It is worth noting that so far, members of staff were not specifically trained to deal with mental health issues. In 1808, a bill was passed to regulate the treatment of mental health patients.</p>
<p>In America, Dorothea Lynda Dix introduced reforms after visiting Britain and seeing how mentally sick persons were improving after getting reformed type of management. In 1841, she managed to have a bill passed in parliament to regulate the treatment of the mentally sick in America.</p>
<p>In 1853, Dr. W.A.F Browne started giving informal mental health lectures to nurses so as to give quality care.</p>
<p>By 1882, formal training on mental health had begun in America at McLean Hospital, Boston.</p>
<p>In 1884, formal training in mental health was started in Germany and thereafter other countries followed that example.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-scientific-period">The Scientific Period<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-scientific-period" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The scientific period is associated with the 19th Century. During that period science was devoted to developing modern treatments that were based on scientific findings. Many forms of treatments were discovered and later abandoned like hydrotherapy, insulin therapy and leucotomy.</p>
<p>The current forms of treatments include physical treatment like chemotherapy and electroconvulsive therapy.</p>
<p>There are also various psychological treatments, which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Individual/group psychotherapy</li>
<li>Behavior therapy</li>
<li>Occupational therapy</li>
<li>Rehabilitation</li>
<li>Cognitive therapy</li>
<li>Counseling</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Some of these treatments will be covered in more detail in section two of this unit</p>
<p>The scientific period witnessed the integration of mental health services with other health services. Trained manpower was developed to care for the mentally sick.</p>
<p>Men and women were either managed separately or in the same wards, depending on the policy of the particular hospital.</p>
<p>Children were managed in special wards.</p>
<p>Where resources were available, different mental health conditions were managed in different units</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="development-of-psychiatry-and-mental-health-services-in-kenya">Development of Psychiatry and Mental Health Services in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#development-of-psychiatry-and-mental-health-services-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The current Mathari hospital was started in July 1910 as a lunatic asylum(place for housing the insane). Before then, the facility served as a smallpox isolation centre. The asylum was renamed Mathari Mental Hospital in 1924. The care was mainly custodial, taking place in dark, gloomy and often damp conditions.</p>
<p>Europeans, Africans, and Asians were managed separately and the quality of mental health care provided depended on the individual's racial background.</p>
<p>Mathari was the only mental hospital until the 1962 Decentralization of Mental Health Services Act. Other facilities began to spring up, including a 22 bed psychiatric unit in Nakuru in 1962, Machakos in 1963, Nyeri and Muranga in 1964 and Port Reitz and Kakamega in 1965.</p>
<p>Currently all provincial hospitals have operational psychiatric units. However, only some district hospitals have operational psychiatric units. Outpatient psychiatric clinics have been established in most of the district hospitals.</p>
<p>Mathari hospital is being redeveloped, and the future plan is to intensify community based psychiatric services all over the country. It is worth noting that community psychiatric services were established in Nairobi in 1983.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training-of-mental-health-workers">Training of Mental Health Workers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training-of-mental-health-workers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The training of enrolled psychiatric nurses was started in 1961 and later changed to a post enrolled psychiatric nursing course. In 1963, the first two registered psychiatric nurses were trained overseas.</p>
<p>In 1979, a post basic diploma in psychiatric nursing was started in Kenya. Between 1972 and 1982 most psychiatrists received overseas training at the Institute of Psychiatry in England.</p>
<p>In 1982, the University of Nairobi started training psychiatrists.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-that-influence-attitudes-towards-mental-health-and-mental-illness">Factors that Influence Attitudes towards Mental Health and Mental Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-influence-attitudes-towards-mental-health-and-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Having outlined the classification of mental illness, you will now turn your attention to the factors that influence attitudes towards mental health and mental illness. In this section, you are going to look at just a few examples.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="culture">Culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The way people think, behave or feel is shaped by their culture. Culture also determines the features of insanity, for example, who is labeled as insane and under what circumstances.</p>
<p>What is considered insane in one culture may be considered perfectly normal in another. Culture also gives guidelines on the nature of treatment and the identity of the helper.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="education">Education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The level of education also influences attitudes towards mental health and mental illness.</p>
<p>An educated person has a better understanding of health and mental illness, thus making their attitude more positive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-beliefs">Health Beliefs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-beliefs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These will determine whether the individual's attitude is positive or negative. It will depend on how the patient explains the illness to themselves, that is, whether they believe in germ theory, evil spirits or an imbalance of some kind.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="religion">Religion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#religion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A patient's reaction to mental illness will often depend on whether or not the patient believes in God or a particular religion, for example, some religions believe that ill health is caused by evil spirits. Usually, religion encourages the followers to be empathetic to</p>
<p>sick people.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stigma-and-mental-disorders">STIGMA AND MENTAL DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stigma-and-mental-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mental illness can cause severe disability and suffering to patients, their relatives and society. Living with a mentally ill person leads to restrictions of social and leisure activities not only for the mentally ill, but for the whole family.</p>
<p>Mentally ill people and their relatives are usually rejected and stigmatized by the society.</p>
<p>Stigma: the feelings of disapproval that people have about particular illnesses or way of behaving.</p>
<p>Stigma related to mental illness is in three forms:</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient may be stigmatized by health care providers, relatives and society.</li>
<li>The relatives also experience stigma from society given that some communities associate mental illness with a curse or taboo.</li>
</ul>
<p>Popular attitudes towards the mentally ill are deep seated and can be seen in the stigmatizing language that is often used to describe people who are mentally ill—“nuts” or “pyscho”. Some people still refer to psychiatric hospitals as “nuthouses”.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="myths-on-mental-illness">MYTHS ON MENTAL ILLNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myths-on-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>People with mental illness cannot work</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: people with mental illness work, even if they have these symptoms. Work is a vital part of rehabilitation; it increases self-esteem, reconnects the ill person to the community and provides a meaningful way to fill time.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>People with mental illness are violent</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: mental disorders and violence are closely linked in the public mind. The stereotype of the violent mental patient causes public fear and avoidance of the mentally ill. People with mental illness in general are no more dangerous than healthy individuals from the same population.</li>
<li>Things to keep in mind about the stereotype (thoughts and beliefs that do not reflect reality) of violence:</li>
<li>Treatment dramatically reduces the risk of violence.</li>
<li>The risk of violence is not necessarily due to illness, but a combination of disorders.</li>
<li>The violence associated with mental illness is most often directed at a family member.</li>
<li>People with mental illness do not pose a risk to children.</li>
<li>The risk of violence in persons with mental illnesses appears to be very similar to that in the healthy population, when substance abuse is factored out.</li>
<li>The contribution of those with mental illness to the overall incidence is relatively small.</li>
<li>The risk of sexual offences associated with mental illness is low.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>All people with mental illness are mentally retarded</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: mental illness and mentally retardation are entirely different conditions. Most mental illnesses occur in people of all levels of intelligence and often in talented and creative people.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Jail is an appropriate place for people with mental illness</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: jail and prison do not have psychiatry services. Mentally ill prisoners receive little or no treatment. Moreover, they are subjected to “double punishment.” If they are housed with the general prison population, their abnormal behavior leads to beating and abuse by other prisoners. If they are segregated for their protection, they lose all social contact and the isolation often worsens their symptoms.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>People never recover from a psychotic illness</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: this misconception leads to hopelessness and despair. It may cause some families to neglect or abandon ill relatives. This disorder takes many different courses with varying outcomes. Some people have episodes of illness lasting weeks or months with full remission of their symptom between each episode; others have a fluctuating course in which symptoms are continuous, but rise and fall in intensity; others have very little variation in the symptoms of their illness over time. At the end some people with psychosis recover completely from the illness—all their psychotic symptoms disappear and they return to their previous level of functioning. Others continue to have symptoms, but are able to lead satisfying and productive lives, while others do not recover.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Mental illness is contagious</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: fear of contagion results in people avoiding those who have a mental disorder. Fear of contagion also leads to stigmatization of family members, mental health professionals and places of treatment.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="7">
<li>Mental illness is caused by evil spirits or witchcraft</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: there is a multitude of misconceptions about the cause of mental illness, but mental disorder is not caused by a curse or an "evil eye," God's punishment for family sins or lack of faith in God or reading too many books. It's not a form of demonic possession.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="8">
<li>People with mental illness are not able to make decisions about their own treatment</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fact: most people with mental illness are able and eager to participate in decision-making about their treatment. During the onset of the illness or during periods of relapse, people may have some difficulty with decision-making.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reducing-stigma-and-discrimination">REDUCING STIGMA AND DISCRIMINATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reducing-stigma-and-discrimination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Increase use of treatment strategies that control symptoms, while avoiding the side effects.</li>
<li>Initiate community educational activities aimed at changing attitudes toward people with mental illness.</li>
<li>Include ant stigma education in the training of teachers and health care providers.</li>
<li>Improve psychoeducation of patients and families about ways of living with disease.</li>
<li>Involve patient and families in identifying the discriminatory practices.</li>
<li>Put emphasis on development of medications that improve the quality of life and minimize stigmatizing side effects.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-and-qualities-of-psychiatric-nursing">Principles and Qualities of Psychiatric Nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-and-qualities-of-psychiatric-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="respect-for-the-patient">Respect for the Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#respect-for-the-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is achieved by accepting the patient as they are.</p>
<p>The therapist should take time to listen to the patient and provide privacy for all conversations.</p>
<p>Minimise situations and experiences that might humiliate the patient and be honest in providing information on medicines, privileges, length of management and stays in hospital if indicated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="availability">Availability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#availability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The nurse must be constantly available to assist the patient to attain their basic needs and alleviate suffering.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="spontaneity">Spontaneity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spontaneity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You should avoid being overly formal. Instead, you should be comfortable with yourself, be flexible and aware of the therapeutic goals.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="acceptance">Acceptance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acceptance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Even if the patient behaves in a way that does not please the nurse, they should be accepted as they are, but taking care not to reinforce their behaviour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sensitivity">Sensitivity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensitivity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You should do your best to show genuine interest and concern.</p>
<p>You should be persistent and patient even if no observable improvement is made.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="accountability">Accountability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#accountability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Since mentally ill patients are vulnerable due to their distorted thinking and behaviour, accountability is required more in a psychiatric setting than any other type of health care (Peplau, cited by Wilson and Kneisl, 1988). You are also accountable to yourself as well as professional colleagues and peers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="empathy">Empathy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#empathy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is the process of putting yourself in another's shoes and remaining emotionally detached. The nurse should strive to understand the patient's perspective, and work toward mutually developed goals.</p>
<p>This document is available on
5 | Page
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The most important function of empathy is that it enables you to give the patient the feeling of being understood and cared about.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="self-understanding">Self-understanding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#self-understanding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This involves recognition and acceptance of your own behaviour and how it affects your relationship with other people. This will inevitably help you, as a therapist, to understand other peoples' behaviour, needs and problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="permissiveness-and-firmness">Permissiveness and Firmness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#permissiveness-and-firmness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Although you have been told to accept the patient as they are, this does not mean that you are in a position to allow them to do whatever they like. The therapist is expected to set limits and to be firm in implementing them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skill-in-observation">Skill in Observation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skill-in-observation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is important for a psychiatric nurse to be alert and observant at all times of the patient's behaviour, attitudes and how they react to staff, relatives and fellow patients.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychopathology">PSYCHOPATHOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychopathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="aetiological-factors-of-mental-illness">AETIOLOGICAL FACTORS OF MENTAL ILLNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiological-factors-of-mental-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Many factors are responsible for the causation of mental illness. These factors may predispose an individual to mental illness, precipitate or perpetuate the mental illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These factors determine an individual's susceptibility to mental illness. They are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Genetic make-up.</li>
<li>Physical damage to the CNS.</li>
<li>Adverse psychosocial influence.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="precipitating-factors">Precipitating factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precipitating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are events that occur shortly before the onset of a disorder and appear to have induced it. They are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Physical stress.</li>
<li>Psychological stress.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="perpetuating-factors">Perpetuating factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perpetuating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These factors are responsible for aggravating or prolonging the diseases already existing in an individual.</p>
<p>Etiological factors of mental illness can be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Biological factors.</li>
<li>Physiological changes.</li>
<li>Psychological factors.</li>
<li>Social factors.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-biological-factors">A. Biological factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-biological-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-heredity">1. Heredity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-heredity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What one inherits is not the illness or its symptoms, but a predisposition to the illness, which is determined by the genes that we inherit directly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-brain-damage">2. Brain damage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-brain-damage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Any damage to the structure and functioning of the brain can give rise to mental illness. Damage to the structure of the brain may be due to one of the following causes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Infection: neurosyphyllis, encephalitis, HIV infection.</li>
<li>Injury: resulting in loss of brain tissue due to brain injury.</li>
<li>Intoxication: damage to brain tissue due to toxins such as alcohol, barbiturates.</li>
<li>Vascular: poor blood supply, bleeding.</li>
<li>Alteration in brain function: changes in blood chemistry that interfere with brain functioning such as disturbance in blood glucose levels, hypoxia, anoxia, fluid and electrolyte imbalance.</li>
<li>Brain tumors.</li>
<li>Vitamin deficiency and malnutrition, in particular deficiency of vitamin B complex.</li>
<li>Degenerative diseases: dementia.</li>
<li>Endocrine disturbances: hypothyroidism, thyrotoxicosis.</li>
<li>Physical defects and physical illness: results in loss of mental capacities.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-biochemical-factors">3. Biochemical factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-biochemical-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Disturbance in neurotransmitters in the brain is found to play an important role in the etiology of certain psychiatric disorders.</li>
<li>Neurotransmitters play an essential function in the role of human emotion and behaviour. They are chemicals that convey information across the synaptic cleft to neighboring target cells.</li>
<li>Major categories of neurotransmitters include: cholinergics, amino acids, monoamines and neuropeptides.</li>
</ul>

<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
