<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-physiological-changes">B. Physiological changes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-physiological-changes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It has been observed that mental disorders are more likely to occur at certain critical periods of life namely: puberty, menstruation, pregnancy, delivery, and puerperium.</li>
<li>These periods are marked not only by physiological (endocrine) changes, but also by psychological issues that diminish the adaptive capacity of the individual.</li>
<li>Thus an individual becomes more susceptible to mental illness during this period.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-psychological-factors">C. Psychological factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-psychological-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is observed that some specific personality types are more prone to develop certain psychological disorders. E.g. unsocial and reserved.</li>
<li>Strained interpersonal relationships at home, place of work, school or college, bereavement, loss of prestige, loss of job.</li>
<li>Childhood insecurities due to parents with pathological personalities, faulty attitude of parents (over strictness, over leniency), abnormal parent child relationship (over protection, rejection, unhealthy comparisons), deprivation of child’s essential psychological and social needs.</li>
<li>Social and recreational deprivations resulting in boredom, isolation and alienation.</li>
<li>Marriage problems like forced bachelorhood, disharmony due to physical, emotional, social, educational or financial incompatibility, childlessness, too many children.</li>
<li>Sexual difficulties arising out of improper sex education, unhealthy attitudes towards sexual functions, pre- and extra-marital sex relations, worries about sexual perversions.</li>
<li>Stress, frustration and seasonal variations are sometimes noted in the occurrence of mental diseases.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-factors">Social factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Poverty, unemployment, injustice, insecurity, immigration, urbanization.</li>
<li>Gambling, alcoholism, prostitution, broken homes, divorce, very big family, religion, traditions, political upheavals and other social crises.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychiatric-interview-assessment-and-classification">PSYCHIATRIC INTERVIEW, ASSESSMENT AND CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychiatric-interview-assessment-and-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-psychiatric-interview">THE PSYCHIATRIC INTERVIEW<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-psychiatric-interview" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This interview is the most important tool in psychiatry. It is used to understand the patient’s problem, elicit signs and symptoms, make appropriate diagnosis, initiate treatment and predict outcome.</li>
<li>Offers patients an opportunity to express themselves and others in a non-critical and non-judgmental atmosphere.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-why-a-patient-consults-a-mental-health-worker">REASONS WHY A PATIENT CONSULTS A MENTAL HEALTH WORKER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-why-a-patient-consults-a-mental-health-worker" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Due to disturbing experiences</li>
<li>Pressure from the family, relatives, friends or the employer.</li>
<li>Others may be forced through the courts.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-setting-of-the-psychiatric-interview">THE SETTING OF THE PSYCHIATRIC INTERVIEW<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-setting-of-the-psychiatric-interview" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Should provide privacy and assure confidentiality.</li>
<li>The patient should receive full attention of the medial practitioner.</li>
<li>The sitting positions determine how the interview proceeds and what is said during the interview.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient to sit at right angles to the clinician with the distance between the patient and the clinician permitting easy communication without shouting and at the same time avoiding the discomfort of close physical proximity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-principles-in-psychiatric-interviews">GENERAL PRINCIPLES IN PSYCHIATRIC INTERVIEWS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-principles-in-psychiatric-interviews" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Active observation and awareness behavior</p>
<p>This begins from the moment the patient walks into the consultation room.</p>
<p>The gait, the physical appearance and greetings, as well as the general attitude to the interview are all important. Focus on verbal and non-verbal communication.</p>
<p>Assessment and evaluation is a two-way process</p>
<p>While the medical worker is assessing the patient, the patient is also evaluating the medical worker on sensitivity and genuine desire to help. The patient may not reveal a great deal about himself unless he senses that the clinician is interested and concerned about him.</p>
<p>If for instance the clinician looks at his watch, it may give the impression that he finds the patient boring.</p>
<p>Acceptance of the behavior of the patient</p>
<p>All behavior including what appears at first sight as odd has a meaning to the patient.</p>
<p>Such behavior may invite ridicule and laughter. The clinician should accept such odd behavior.</p>
<p>Accepting does not however mean approving it.</p>
<p>Avoid arguments with the patient</p>
<p>Avoid getting drawn into an argument with the patient. It may the patient’s way of relating to others or seeking help. The clinician should try to find the underlying relationship problems.</p>
<p>Do not assume you understand the patient</p>
<p>At all times the clinician should make sure he understands what the patient says or feels.</p>
<p>Very often what the patient expresses may be about problems close to our own, e.g. ordinary feelings like depression. One has to find the depth of the depression, whether he cries, has feelings of hopelessness and suicidal thoughts and the presence or absence of associated symptoms, such as change in appetite and weight, and disturbance of sleep.</p>
<p>One method of clarifying one’s thoughts of what the patient says and feel, is for the clinician to summarize a number of times during the interview by repeating what the patient has said and the feelings the patient has expressed. The patient can correct the clinician if he has been misunderstood.</p>
<p>Stress on feelings</p>
<p>The feeling of the patient may be difficult for the new clinician to understand. First the beginner may feel awkward and at a loss of what to do with an outpouring of feelings for example crying by the patient.</p>
<p>The patient should be offered the opportunity to unburden these feelings, which may have a cathartic effect.</p>
<p>The second dilemma encountered by novices is when a patient talks about suicidal feelings. For example, they may end up suggesting it to the patients.</p>
<p>The important point is when and how to ask such questions.</p>
<p>When the patient is telling the clinician his feelings of hopelessness, posing such a question such as “don’t you think of suicide?” is not appropriate.</p>
<p>It would be appropriate to ask, “When you feel so low, do you feel sometimes feel that life is not worth living?” and to proceed from there.</p>
<p>The clinician should focus on feelings and emotionally charged areas should be explored. At times the patient may show resistance and these should be kept in mind for further discussion later in the interview.</p>
<p>Sensitive topics should be handled carefully and tactfully. Introduce them gradually.</p>
<p>Focus on interpersonal relationships</p>
<p>Apart from the usual information about family history, the important areas are the interpersonal sense of love, acceptance, security and discipline. These facts reveal factors responsible in shaping the personality of the patient.</p>
<p>Avoid being moralistic or judgmental</p>
<p>Some patients may come to the interview, expecting the worst with a great deal of anxiety or guilt.</p>
<p>That is one of the main reasons why people avoid sharing their problems and feelings.</p>
<p>Show empathy</p>
<p>This is sensing the client’s inner world of private personal meaning as if it were your own, but without losing the “as if” quality.</p>
<p>Try to tolerate the silence</p>
<p>10 | Page</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The novice may find it difficult when the patient does not respond to the posed question right away. The period of silence may be as a result of the patient trying to sort out his thoughts, or the patient may not wish to respond to that particular question, probably due to illness itself or feeling aroused.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-stages-of-a-psychiatric-interview">THE STAGES OF A PSYCHIATRIC INTERVIEW<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-stages-of-a-psychiatric-interview" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-initial-phase">The initial phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-initial-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This phase begins from the first contact with the patient. The clinician should greet the patient and introduce himself. Both of them should sit comfortably. Questions should be open ended and simple. Those that begin with “why” are usually difficult to answer, and creates distance, thus should be avoided. Avoid technical terms. The initial phase mainly covers the patient’s illness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-middle-phase">The middle phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-middle-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>This part of the interview focuses on the background of the patient, his upbringing, family life, educational and vocational life and interpersonal relationships, both past and present. The clinician tries to find out the influences of these factors on personality and current problems of the patient.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="closing-phase">Closing phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#closing-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>It is important to give the patient some minutes before closing the interview to ask questions or express the points that were not covered during the interview.</p>
<p>Questions such as “before we finish for the day, is there any question you wanted to ask?” or “are there any points which you feel that you wanted to discuss now?”</p>
<p>This may open new areas for interview. The patient may raise points already discussed showing the areas of his particular concern. Discuss the patient’s areas of concern and the feelings associated with it.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-psychiatric-assessment-history">THE PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT/HISTORY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-psychiatric-assessment-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is obtained from the parent as well as from the family, relatives or friends. This is because in some cases the patient may not be responsive or may be confused and in others the history given by the patient may be inaccurate.</p>
<p>An alcoholic, for example, tends to conceal his drinking or a schizophrenic patient may not reveal his abnormal experiences, such as delusions or hallucinations.</p>
<p>An accurate history and MSE are the cornerstones of diagnoses and treatment in psychiatry.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="when-do-you-write-the-psychiatric-history">WHEN DO YOU WRITE THE PSYCHIATRIC HISTORY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-do-you-write-the-psychiatric-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is best to write the entire history and MSE at the end of the session. However note down important points like dates, presence of psychopathological symptoms as it may be difficult to recall this later.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="when-do-you-interview-the-family">WHEN DO YOU INTERVIEW THE FAMILY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-do-you-interview-the-family" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In severely disturbed patients, it is important to involve the family during the initial interview. So much information may be obtained from the family, which may not be readily available from the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-the-psychiatric-history">COMPONENTS OF THE PSYCHIATRIC HISTORY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-the-psychiatric-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="personal-identifying-data">Personal / Identifying Data<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-identifying-data" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Here you ask for information pertaining to age, sex, marital status, occupation, residence and nationality.</p>
<p>The referral system</p>
<p>Note the source of referral, whether by a health worker, brought by family members or self-accord indicating the main reasons for referral.</p>
<p>Chief complaint</p>
<p>This is a brief statement of why the patient seeks help. It should contain the description of the problem and should be stated in the patient’s own word. Where a patient does not see himself as needing help or in the case of a patient being unable or unwilling to speak, C.C can be obtained from relatives. The so</p>
<p>This document is available on
11 | Page
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="history-of-presenting-illness">History of Presenting Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-of-presenting-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The patient’s problems are explored in detail and in chronological order. It starts from the time when the patient started feeling the discomfort, which may predate on his social interactions with others both at home or at work, its consequences on his family and his occupation are investigated.</p>
<p>Other symptoms associated with the chief complaints are documented in this section.</p>
<p>This should contain the psychosocial stress factors in the life of the patient, as well as physical illness and their time relationship with the presenting symptoms. Ask the patient about the onset of the illness, duration, any allegations that brought them to the mental hospital and the patient’s pre-morbid history, that is, how they presented before they became mentally ill.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In an outpatient clinic, this information is better taken first, since the patient or the informant would like to talk about it straight away.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="past-medical-and-psychiatric-history">Past Medical and Psychiatric History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#past-medical-and-psychiatric-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By taking down the patient’s medical history, you are in a position to find out about any medical conditions the patient has suffered, which may have affected their mental health.</p>
<p>You should also try and find out if there have been any incidences of the patient being admitted into a mental unit/hospital and the outcome of the treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family-history">Family History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The components of the family history depend on the type of family and its composition. For each family member it is important to note the name, age, sex, marital status, occupation and their relationship, past and present, with the patient and state their current health condition. Find out if the parents or any of the siblings are partially or totally economically dependent on the patient and how he feels about it. Find out if there is any family history of mental illness among the nuclear or extended family.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-history">Personal History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The past period of the life of the patient should be reviewed. The aim is to obtain a comprehensive picture of the patient and to find out factors in his past which may explain his psychological make-up, personality and present problems. Maybe divided into the following periods:</p>
<p><strong>Pregnancy, birth and early development up to around 6 years</strong></p>
<p>The interviewer should ask the following questions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Was the pregnancy unwanted, or out of wedlock and what were the consequences on the relationship of mother and child and other members of the family?</li>
<li>Was there any problem during pregnancy and delivery?</li>
<li>Was it an extended or nuclear family? In the case of an extended family, who in the family was closely attending to the patient’s needs? The interpersonal relationship of the individuals in the family unit, its cohesiveness, and the social economic situation of the family should be investigated.</li>
</ul>
<p>Have there been significant incidents in the family like separation, divorce, illness and death of significant people? Was there any problem with separation and socialization? How was the performance at school? Were there any neurotic traits like nail biting and thumb sucking?</p>
<p><strong>Six years to puberty</strong></p>
<p>This section focuses on the individual sense of identity, participation in structured activities, whether they liked school, their school performance, type of discipline and attitude towards authority (both at home and in school), peer group activities and its influence on the patient as well as coping mechanisms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adolescence-to-19-years">Adolescence to 19 years<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adolescence-to-19-years" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a period of heightened sexual awareness. Social achievements and relationships both at home and in school with other students and teachers should be explored. What are the patient’s professional interests and future goals, involvement in any extra-curricular activities? Daily activities and social contacts are explored for the patient who did not go to school.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="occupational-history">Occupational history<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#occupational-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The age and which work the patient first engaged in, any income generating activity or employment, the nature of work, social and occupational relationships, jobsatisfaction, growth and improvement or deterioration in the job are considered.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Repeated absenteeism from work or deterioration of work activity, for example, may indicate alcoholism, depression or schizophrenia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="marital-history">Marital history<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marital-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The interviewer should ask the age when the patient got married, whether the marriage was a personal decision was a personal decision or arranged by the family and the individual’s feelings towards the marriage. If the decision was personal one, a negative reaction to the marriage by one or both families may have a significant impact. The health and personality of the marriage partner plays an important role in the relationship. The birth dates of children, their health and educational achievements are assessed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-history">Sexual History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Extra care is necessary in interviewing patients about their sexual life. The clinician should try to elicit information without embarrassing the patient. If the patient presents with sexual problems, a detailed sexual history is necessary. The patient attitude towards sex, the sexual partners, sexual experiences in the past, its frequency, the moral and religious attitude of the patient and the feelings associated with it, the areas to evaluate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mental-status-assessment-examination">Mental Status Assessment/ Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-status-assessment-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is used to determine whether a patient is experiencing abnormalities in thinking and reasoning ability, feelings or behaviour.</p>
<p>Check facial expressions to provide information about mood, orientation to time, place, person, concentration and perceptual disorder, where you should check for the following senses:</p>
<ul>
<li>Olfactory</li>
<li>Auditory</li>
<li>Tactile</li>
<li>Visual</li>
<li>Gustatory</li>
</ul>
<p>The following outline is generally accepted in reporting MSE findings:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-appearance">General appearance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-appearance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Note the grooming, posture, gait, physical characteristics, facial expression, eye contact, motor activity and specific mannerisms. Note the state of awareness or consciousness, stupor, delirium, fleeting consciousness and coma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="speech">Speech<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#speech" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Note the rate, pitch, volume, clarity, speech abnormalities such as dysarthria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mood">Mood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Refer to expression of emotion, which is subjective. Note the variability or range, intensity and appropriateness. Mood could be described as dysphoric, euthymic, expansive, irritable, labile, elevated, euphoric, ecstatic, depressive or an hedonic.</p>
<p><strong>Affect</strong> is said to be appropriate or inappropriate, blunted, restricted, flat or labile.</p>
<p>In some cases the patient may have difficulty expressing feelings or emotions referred to as alexithymia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thoughts">Thoughts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thoughts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Two components of thoughts are assessed: the thought process and the thought content.</p>
<p>Thought process includes the flow of ideas and quality of associations; the process of thinking should include rate and flow of ideas. Thoughts can be racing or totally slowed down. There may be circumstantiality, blocking or perseveration as occurs in schizophrenia. Thought broadcasting and insertion are pathogenic features of schizophrenia.</p>
<p>Associations defined as the relationships between ideas can be exhibited by loosening, flight of ideas, neologisms, word salad or echolalia.</p>
<p>Thought content includes distortions, delusions, ideas of reference, depersonalization, derealization, preoccupations, obsessions, phobias, somatic concerns, suicidal or homicidal ideation. In suicidal and homicidal ideation the interviewer needs to assess the thoughts, plans, feelings and potential for actions and deterrents to action.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="perception">Perception<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Enquiries about perceptual disturbances require careful approach and should evaluate the presence or absence of illusions, hallucinations, depersonalization or derealization. Hallucinations should focus on all the five sense organs (sight, hearing, taste, touch and smell) involved, with their contact, frequency and circumstances of their occurrence are recorded.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cognitive-functions">COGNITIVE FUNCTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cognitive-functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sensorium">Sensorium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensorium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disturbance of consciousness usually denotes organic brain conditions. Determine the level of consciousness and any fluctuations if present. This may range from mild clouding of consciousness to stupor or coma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="orientation">Orientation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orientation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is to check if the patient knows the time, place and person. Does the patient know time of the day, of the week, month and year? The responses expected are determined by the social and cultural background of the patients. For place, ask about familiar places. For person, ask about his name, age, name of children, parents and siblings. These should be counter checked with family members.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="attention-and-concentration">Attention and concentration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attention-and-concentration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Naming three objects to the patient or giving a telephone number which the patient is told to repeat after the interviewer can assess whether they are attentive. By this time the interview process one can gauge a patient's attention span by how they answer the questions and their participation in the whole process.</p>
<p>On the other hand, concentration can be determined using simple calculations like subtracting 7 from 100 (serial seven) up to 65 or 3 from 20 (serial three) or by means of simple problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="memory">Memory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#memory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Memory is assessed in three categories: immediate (recall), recent and remote.</p>
<p>Immediate memory, which pertains to retention and recall involves events occurring in the last few seconds to minutes, can be assessed by giving the patient telephone numbers with 5 to 6 digits and asking them to repeat.</p>
<p>Recent memory is hours to 2-3 days, thus involves asking patients what they ate for breakfast or where they were in the last few days.</p>
<p>Remote memory involves past years events. Important family or historic dates in the patient's socio-cultural context may be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intelligence">Intelligence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intelligence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Use IQ.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="judgment">Judgment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Does the patient understand the harmful consequences of his behavior to himself, the family and community? Would the patient make wise decisions, for example, in case of fire, drowning or any life threatening situation?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="insight">Insight<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insight" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The awareness of the patient about his illness and its implication varies depending on whether the patient is psychotic or non-psychotic. The psychotic is said to have insight if he realizes that he is sick and that his delusions and hallucinations are normal experiences.</p>
<p>A neurotic on the other hand is said to have insight if he understands that that his symptoms are due to environmental factors or internal emotional causes.</p>
<p>14 | Page</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychiatric-classification">PSYCHIATRIC CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychiatric-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are two main sets of classification used in psychiatry:</p>
<p>The international classification of diseases version 10 (ICD-10) chapter 5 by the WHO.</p>
<p>The diagnostic and statistical manual for mental disorders, 4th edition (DSM-IV TR)</p>
<p>We will adopt DSM-IV TR classification. Its multiaxial approach is described in detail below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="multiaxial-assessment">MULTIAXIAL ASSESSMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#multiaxial-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A multiaxial system involves an assessment on several axes, each of which refers to a different domain of information that may help a clinician plan treatment and predict outcome.</p>
<p>There are 5 axes included in the DSM-IV multiaxial classification:</p>
<ul>
<li>Axis 1: clinical disorders</li>
<li>Other conditions that may be a focus of clinical attention</li>
<li>Axis II: personality disorders.</li>
<li>Mental retardation</li>
<li>Axis III: general medical conditions.</li>
<li>Axis IV: psychosocial and environmental problems.</li>
<li>Axis V: global assessment of functioning.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="axis-1-clinical-disorders">AXIS 1: CLINICAL DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#axis-1-clinical-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Other conditions that may be a focus of clinical attention.</p>
<p>Axis 1 is for reporting all the various disorders or conditions in the classification except for personality disorders and mental retardation (axis II). Also reported on axis I are other conditions that may be a focus of clinical attention.</p>
<p>Examples:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disorders usually first diagnosed in infancy, childhood or adolescence (excluding mental retardation)</li>
<li>Delirium, dementia, amnesia (cognitive disorders)</li>
<li>Mental disorders due to a general medical condition.</li>
<li>Substance related disorders.</li>
<li>Schizophrenia and other psychotic disorders.</li>
<li>Mood disorders. (affective disorders; major depression and bipolar)</li>
<li>Anxiety disorders.</li>
<li>Somatoform disorders.</li>
<li>Factitious disorders.</li>
<li>Dissociative disorders.</li>
<li>Sexual and gender identity disorders.</li>
<li>Eating disorders.</li>
<li>Sleep disorders.</li>
<li>Impulse control disorders.</li>
<li>Adjustment disorders.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other conditions that may be a focus of clinical attention.</p>
<p>When an individual has more than one Axis I disorder, all of these should be reported if more than Axis I disorder is present, the principle diagnosis or the reason for visit should be indicated by listing it first.</p>
<p>When an individual has both Axis I and an Axis II disorder, the principal diagnosis or the reason for the visit will be assumed to be on Axis I unless the Axis II diagnosis is followed by the qualifying phrase “(principal diagnosis)” or “reason for visit.”</p>
<p>If no Axis I disorder is deferred, pending the gathering of additional information, this should also be stated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="axis-ii-personality-disorders">AXIS II: PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#axis-ii-personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mental retardation</li>
</ul>
<p>This is for reporting personality disorders and mental retardation. It may also be used for noting prominent maladaptive personality features and defence mechanisms.</p>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>When an individual has both Axis I and Axis II diagnosis and the Axis II is the principal diagnosis or the main reason for visit, this should be indicated by adding the qualifying phrase “(principal diagnosis)” or “(reason for visit)” after the Axis II diagnosis.</p>
<ul>
<li>Examples</li>
<li>Paranoid,</li>
<li>Schizoid</li>
<li>Schizotypal</li>
<li>Antisocial</li>
<li>Borderline</li>
<li>Histrionic</li>
<li>Narcissitic</li>
<li>Avoidant</li>
<li>Dependent</li>
<li>Obsessive compulsive</li>
<li>Personality</li>
<li>Specified</li>
<li>Mental retardation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="axis-iii-general-medical-conditions">AXIS III: GENERAL MEDICAL CONDITIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#axis-iii-general-medical-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is for reporting current general medical conditions that are potentially relevant to the understanding or management of the individuals’s mental disorder.</p>
<p>The purpose of distinguishing GMC is to encourage thoroughness in evaluation and to enhance communication among health care providers.</p>
<p>GMC can be related to mental disorders in various ways.</p>
<p>In some cases it may be related directly to the aetiological development or worsening of the mental symptoms and that the mechanism for this effect is physiological.</p>
<p>When a mental disorder is judged to be a direct physiological consequence of the GMC, a mental disorder due to a GMC should be diagnosed on Axis I and the GMC should be recorded on both Axes I and III.</p>
<p>In those instances in which the aetiological relationship between the GMC and the mental symptoms is insufficiently clear to warrant Axis I diagnosis of mental disorder due to a GMC, the appropriate mental disorder (e.g major depressive disorder) should be listed and coded on Axis I; the GMC should only be coded on Axis III.</p>
<p>There are other situations in which the GMC are recorded on Axis III because of their importance to the overall understanding or treatment of the individual with mental disorder:</p>
<ul>
<li>An Axis I disorder maybe a psychological reaction to an Axis III.</li>
<li>Some GMC may not be directly related to a mental disorder but nonetheless have important prognostic or treatment implications.</li>
<li>The choice of pharmacotherapy is influenced by the GMC.</li>
</ul>
<p>When an individual has more than one clinically relevant Axis III diagnosis, all should be reported.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="axis-iv-psychosocial-and-environmental-problems">AXIS IV: PSYCHOSOCIAL AND ENVIRONMENTAL PROBLEMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#axis-iv-psychosocial-and-environmental-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is for reporting psychosocial and environmental problems that may affect the diagnosis, treatment and prognosis of mental disorders (Axes I and II).</p>
<p>When an individual has multiple psychosocial or environmental problems, the health worker may note as many as are judged to be relevant. Only those that have been present during the year preceding the current evaluation should be noted.</p>
<p>You may also note those occurring prior to the previous year if these clearly contribute to the mental disorder or have become a focus for treatment.</p>
<p>In practice, most psychosocial and environmental problems will be indicated on Axis IV. However, when it is the primary focus of clinical attention, it should also be recorded on Axis I.</p>
<p>They are grouped in the following categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Problems with primary support group:</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Death of a family member; health problems in the family; disruption of family by separation; divorce, or enstrangement; removal from the home, remarriage of parent; sexual or physical abuse; parental overprotection; neglect of child; inadequate discipline; discord with siblings; birth of a sibling.</p>
<p>Problems related to the social environment:</p>
<p>Death or loss of a friend; inadequate social support; living alone; difficulty with acculturation; discrimination; adjustment to life cycle transition (such as retirement)</p>
<p>Educational problems:</p>
<p>Illiteracy; academic problems; discord with teachers or classmates; inadequate school environment.</p>
<p>Occupational problems:</p>
<p>Unemployment; threat of job loss; stressful work schedule; difficult work conditions; job dissatisfaction; job change; discord with boss or co-workers.</p>
<p>Housing problems:</p>
<p>Homelessness; inadequate housing; unsafe neighbourhood; discord with neighbours or landlord.</p>
<p>Economic problems:</p>
<p>Extreme poverty; inadequate finances; insufficient welfare support.</p>
<p>Problems with access to health care services:</p>
<p>Inadequate health care services; transportation to health care facilities unavailable, inadequate health insurance.</p>
<p>Problems related to interaction with the legal system, crime and arrest:</p>
<p>Incarceration; litigation; victim of crime.</p>
<p>Other psychosocial and environmental problems:</p>
<p>Exposure to disaster, war and other hostilities: discord with non-family care givers such as counselor, social worker or physician; unavailability of social service agencies.</p>
<p>AXIS V: GLOBAL ASSESSMENT OF FUNCTIONING</p>
<p>This is for reporting the clinicians judgement of the individual’s overall level of functioning.</p>
<p>This information is useful in planning treatment and measuring its impact and in predicting outcome.</p>
<p>The reporting of overall functioning on Axis V can be done in using GAF scale.</p>
<p>It is useful in tracking the clinical progress of individual in global terms, using a single measure.</p>
<p>The GAF scale is rated with respect to psychological, social and occupational functioning.</p>
<p>The instructions specify, “do not include impairment in functioning due to physical or environmental limitations”</p>
<p>The GAF scale is divided into 10 ranges of functioning.</p>
<p>Making a GAF rating involves picking a single value that best reflects the individual’s overall level of functioning.</p>
<p>The description of each 10-point range in the GAF scale has two components:</p>
<p>The first part covers the symptom severity, and the second part covers functioning.</p>
<p>In order to ensure that no elements of the GAF scale are overlooked when a rating is being made, the following method may be applied:</p>
<p>STEP 1: start at the top level, evaluate each range each range by asking “is either the individual’s symptom severity or level of functioning worse than what is indicated in the range of description?”</p>
<p>STEP 2: keep moving down the scale until the range that best matches the individual’s symptom severity or the leveling is reached, whichever is worse.</p>
<p>STEP 3: look at the next lower range as a double – check against having stopped prematurely. This range should be too severe on both symptom severity and level of functioning. If it is appropriate range has been reached (continue with step 4) if not, go back to step 2 and continue moving down the scale.</p>
<p>STEP 4: to determine the specific GAF rating within the selected 10-point range, consider whether the individual is functioning at the higher or lower end of the 10-point range. For example, consider an individual who hears voices that do not influence his behaviour.</p>
<p>GAF scale</p>

<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This gives a score that ranges from a possible maximum of 100 to a possible 0 as indicate below.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="code">CODE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#code" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>100-91 superior functioning day in a wide range of activities, life’s problems never seem to get out of hand, is sought out by others because of his many positive qualities. No symptoms.</p>
<p>90-81 absent or minimal symptoms (e.g mild anxiety before an exam), good functioning in all areas, interested and involved in a wide range of activities, socially effective, generally satisfied with life, no more than everyday problems or concerns (e.g an occasional argument with family members)</p>
<p>80-71: If symptoms are present that are transient and expected reactions to psychosocial stressors (e.g difficulty concentrating after family argument); no more than slight impairment in social, occupational or school functioning (e.g. temporarily falling behind in schoolwork)</p>
<p>70-61 some mild symptoms (e.g. depressed mood and mild insomnia) or some difficulty in social, occupational or school functioning (e.g. occasionally truancy, or theft within the household), but generally functioning pretty well, has some meaningful interpersonal relationships.</p>
<p>60-51 moderate symptoms (e.g. flat affect and circumstantial speech, occasional panic attacks) or moderate difficulty in social occupational or school functioning (e.g a few friends, conflicts with peers or co-workers).</p>
<p>50-41 serious symptoms (e.g. suicidal ideation, severe obsessional rituals, frequent shoplifting) or any serious impairment in social, occupational, or school functioning (e.g. no friends, unable to keep a job).</p>
<p>40-31 some impairment in reality testing or communication (e.g. speech is illogical at times, obscure or irrelevant) or major impairment in several areas, such as work or school, family relations, judgement, thinking or mood (e.g. depressed, avoid friends, neglects family, and is unable to work; child frequently beats up younger children, is defiant at home, and is failing at school).</p>
<p>30-21 behaviour is considerably influenced by delusions or hallucinations or serious impairment in communication or judgement (e.g. sometimes incoherent, acts grossly inappropriately, suicidal preoccupation) or inability to function in almost all areas (e.g stays in bed all day; no job, home or friends).</p>
<p>20-11 some danger of hurting self or others (e.g suicide attempts without clear expectations of death; frequently violent; manic excitement) or occasionally fails to maintain minimal personal hygiene (e.g smears faeces) or gross impairment in communication (e.g. largerly incoherent or mute)</p>
<p>10-1 persistent danger of severely hurting self or others (e.g recurrent violence) or persistent inability to maintain minimal personal hygiene or serious suicidal act with clear expectation of death.</p>
<p>0 inadequate information</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-3-treatment-used-in-the-management-of-mentally-ill-persons">SECTION 3: TREATMENT USED IN THE MANAGEMENT OF MENTALLY ILL PERSONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-treatment-used-in-the-management-of-mentally-ill-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-drugs-psychotropics">A. Drugs (psychotropics)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-drugs-psychotropics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are various types of drugs and other physical treatments used to treat patients suffering from mental health illness. These can be grouped together under the following categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antipsychotic Medication</li>
<li>Antidepressant</li>
<li>Anxiolytics and hypnosedatives.</li>
<li>Antiepileptic drugs</li>
<li>Antiparkinsonian Drugs</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at each of these categories in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-antipsychotic-medication">A. Antipsychotic Medication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-antipsychotic-medication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Antipsychotic drugs are also called major tranquilizers or neuroleptics used in the treatment of psychoses like schizophrenia, bipolar disorders (manic phase) and alcohol withdrawal disorder.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="antipsychotic-drugs">Antipsychotic Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanisms-of-action">Mechanisms of Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The drugs are thought to work by blocking dopamine receptors causing a decrease in psychotic symptoms. The drug is metabolised in the liver and excreted by the kidneys. For one to get the desired effects, one must maintain the patient on the lowest dose possible and initial therapy should be on divided doses so that the patient can be monitored.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="for-acutely-psychotic-patients">For acutely psychotic patients:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#for-acutely-psychotic-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Give intramuscular haloperidol, for example, 5mg every 30 to 60 minutes over a two to six hour period. Peak level is attained 20 to 40 minutes after injection.</li>
<li>Monitor blood pressure before each dose and withhold if the systolic blood pressure is 90mm Hg or below.</li>
<li>Sleep state should be monitored to ensure six to seven hours of sleep.</li>
<li>Dystonia occurring 1 hour to 48 hours after starting treatment should be treated with an antiparkinsonism drug.</li>
<li>To decrease the danger to the patient themselves and others, the patient needs to be monitored for possible adverse reactions to the medication.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drugs-should-be-given-using-the-following-time-frame">Drugs should be given using the following time frame:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-should-be-given-using-the-following-time-frame" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Six months for first psychotic episode.</li>
<li>One year period for second psychotic episode.</li>
<li>Indefinite period for third and later psychotic episodes.</li>
<li>The drug should be discontinued through tapering the dosage to avoid dyskinesia.</li>
<li>Gertrude and MacFarland (1986) have identified the following expected responses to the treatment:</li>
<li>Initially the patient is drowsy and co-operative within hours to a week.</li>
<li>The patient becomes more sociable and less withdrawn for the next two months.</li>
<li>The thought disorder generally disappears in six weeks or more.</li>
<li>Improvement is generally noted in hallucinations, acute delusions, sleeping habits, appetite, tension, combativeness, hostility, negativism and personal grooming.</li>
</ul>
