<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Remember:
Use of more than one phenothiazine is not recommended.
Geriatric patients should be given lower dosages to avoid hypertension due to prolonged half-life in people aged over 55 years.</p>
<p>INDICATIONS</p>
<ul>
<li>Organic psychiatric disorders: Delirium, dementia, delirium tremens, drug induced psychosis,</li>
<li>Functional disorders: schizophrenia, schizoaffective disorders, paranoid disorders.</li>
<li>Mood disorders: mania, major depression with psychotic symptoms.</li>
<li>Childhood disorders: attention deficit hyperactivity disorder, autism, enuresis, conduct disorder.</li>
<li>Medical disorders: Huntington’s chorea, nausea and vomiting, tic disorder, eclampsia, severe pain in malignancy, tetanus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Side Effects</p>
<ol>
<li>Extrapyramidal symptoms
These are serious neurologic symptoms and major side effects of antipsychotics. Typical antipsychotics cause a greater incidence of EPS than do atypical antipsychotics.</li>
</ol>
<p>Neuroleptic induced parkinsonism: symptoms include rigidity, tremors, bradykinesia, stooped posture, drooling, akinesia, ataxia. This disorder can be treated with anticholinergic drugs.</p>
<p>Acute dystonia: results from a slow sustained muscular spasm that lead to involuntary movement. Can involve the neck, jaw, tongue and the entire body (opisthotonus). There is also involvement of eyes leading to upward lateral movement of the eyes known as oculogyric crisis. Can be prevented anticholinergics, antihistamines, benzodiazepines.</p>
<p>Akathisia: this is a subjective feeling of muscular discomfort that can cause patients to be agitated, restless and feel generally dysphoric. Can be treated with propranolol, benzodiazepines and clonidine.</p>
<p>Tardive dyskinesia: it is a delayed adverse effect of antipsychotics. It consists of abnormal, irregular choreoathetoid movements of the muscles of the head, limbs and trunk. It is characterized by chewing, sucking, grimacing and perioral movements.</p>
<p>Neuroleptic malignant syndrome: this is a rare but serious disorder occurring in a small minority of patients taking neuroleptics, especially high potency compounds. The onset is usually in the first 10 days of treatment.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Autonomic side effects: Dry mouth, constipation, cyclopedia, mydriasis, urinary retention, orthostatic hypotension, impotence and impaired ejaculation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seizures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sedation.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Other effects: Agranulocytosis, sialorrhoea (increased salivation), weight gain, jaundice, dermatological effects.</p>
<p>NURSE RESPONSIBILITY FOR A PATIENT RECEIVING ANTIPSYCHOTICS</p>
<ul>
<li>Instruct the patient to take sips of water frequently to relieve dryness of mouth.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
6 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>A high fiber diet, increased food intake and laxatives if needed, help to reduce constipation.</li>
<li>Advise patient to get up from the bed or chair very slowly. Patient should sit on the edge of the bed for one full minute dangling his feet before standing up. Check Bp before and after medication is given.</li>
<li>Differentiate between akathisia and agitation and inform the physician. A change of drug may be necessary if side effects are severe. Administer antiparkinsonian as prescribed.</li>
<li>Observe regularly patient regularly for abnormal movements.</li>
<li>Take all seizure precautions.</li>
<li>Patient should be warned about driving or operating machinery when first treated with antipsychotics. Give medications at bedtime to eliminate sedation.</li>
<li>Teach the importance of drug compliance, side effects of the drugs and reporting if too severe, regular follow ups. Give reassurances and reduce unfounded fears and anxiety.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-antidepressants">B. Antidepressants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-antidepressants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These drugs are used to treat depressive disorders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="mechanisms-of-action">Mechanisms of Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>They act by increasing epinephrine and serotonin. Both of them are metabolized in the liver and excreted in the urine.</p>
<p>Table showing some examples of antidepressant drugs.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Major Groups</th><th>Generic Name</th><th>Trade Name</th><th>Daily Dosage (range)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Tricyclic antidepressants</td><td>Amitriptyline</td><td>Elavil (laroxyl)</td><td>75-300mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Imipramine</td><td>Tofranil</td><td>100-300mg</td></tr><tr><td>Tetra cyclic anti-depressants</td><td>Maprotiline</td><td>Ludiomil</td><td>75-300mg</td></tr><tr><td>Monoamine Oxidase Inhibitors</td><td>Isocarboxacid</td><td>Marplan</td><td>10-60mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Phenelzine</td><td>Nardil</td><td>45-90mg</td></tr><tr><td>Selective Serotonin Reuptake Inhibitors</td><td>Fluoxetine</td><td>Prozac</td><td>20mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Citalopram</td><td>Cipramil</td><td>20-60mg</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Paroxetine</td><td>Seroxat</td><td>10-50mg</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="for-the-drugs-to-be-effective">For the drugs to be effective:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#for-the-drugs-to-be-effective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Dosage may be divided, but the total dose can be given at bed time due to the sedative effects.</li>
<li>Minimum dose should be given then increased gradually.</li>
<li>5 to 21 days must be allowed before any mood change is observed.</li>
<li>Four to six weeks must be allowed to pass for therapeutic effects to be observed.</li>
<li>Medication needs to be continued for 6 months after patient is free from depression.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>According to Gertrude and McFarland (1986), some of the side effects that might be experienced include mild anticholinergic effects from tricyclic and monoamine oxidase inhibitors, dry mouth, constipation, blurred vision, tachycardia nausea, edema, hypotension and urinary retention. Adjusting the dosage to a lower level will usually resolve the problem.</p>
<p>Side effects that are specific to tricyclics are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Allergic reactions manifested as skin rash and jaundice.</li>
<li>Tachycardia.</li>
<li>Tremors.</li>
<li>Long term treatment may depress bone marrow, predispose to sore throat and aching, and fever.</li>
<li>Under such circumstances, stopping the use of the drug is the intervention of choice.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Meanwhile, specific side effects of monoamine oxidase inhibitors include:</li>
<li>Liver damage that is rare but fatal.</li>
<li>Precipitation of manic episodes.</li>
<li>Hypertension crisis characterized by severe headache palpitation, neck stiffness, nausea, vomiting, increased Bp, chest pain and collapse. It occurs 30 minutes to 24 hours after eating food containing tyramine. These foods include cheese, wine, beer, sour cream, liver, chocolate, bananas, avocados, soy sauce, and beans.</li>
<li>The main form of treatment when side effects occur is to discontinue the drug and then give regitine to lower the blood pressure.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The use of antidepressants is contraindicated when the patient suffers from glaucoma, agitated states, urinary retention, cardiac disorders and seizure disorders.</p>
<p>Having looked at major tranquilizers and antidepressants, now you will look at minor tranquilizers.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Anti-depressants should be discontinued prior to surgery.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-anxiolytics-or-anti-anxiety-drugs-hypnotics">C. Anxiolytics or Anti-anxiety Drugs / Hypnotics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-anxiolytics-or-anti-anxiety-drugs-hypnotics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These drugs, when given to a patient having generalized anxiety disorder, are able to provide relief.</li>
<li>These are also called minor tranquilizers. Most belong to the BZ group of drugs.</li>
<li>They are mainly recommended for acute anxiety states, which may present with palpitations, sweating, trembling, shortness of breath, chest pain, nausea, dizziness, a feeling of unreality, fear of losing control or dying, chills or numbness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-bz">Classification of BZ<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-bz" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Barbiturates: examples; phenobarbital, pentobarbital, secobarbital and thiopentone.</p>
<p>Non – barbiturate non – benzodiazepine antianxiety agents: for example; Meprobamate glutethimide, ethanol, diphenhydramine and methaqualon.</p>
<p>Benzodiazepines: presently BZ are the drugs of first choice in the treatment of insomnia.</p>
<p>Very short acting: for example, triazolam, midazolam.</p>
<p>Short – acting: example, chlordiazepoxide (Librium), Diazepam (valium, calmpose), clonazepam (lonazepam), Flurazepam (Nindral), Nitrazepam (Dormin)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects">Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main effects include sedation, muscle relaxation and elevation of seizure threshold.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Side effects include dizziness, headache, nervousness, insomnia, light headedness, dry mouth, nausea, vomiting, abdominal and gastric distress and diarrhea.</p>
<p>When high doses of medication are used for more than four months, the patient is likely to develop drug dependence or withdrawal syndrome.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contraindications">Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Benzodiazepines should not be used together with other central nervous system depressants. They should be given with caution to patients who are elderly, depressed or suicidal and those with a history of substance abuse.</p>
<p>It is worth noting that these drugs need to be combined with psychotherapy to ensure complete cure of the problem.</p>
<p>This implies that anxiolytics by themselves are not a cure for psychological problems. The most commonly used drug is diazepam.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>8</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This is usually administered as a dose of 2-10mg bid/qid orally or 2-20mg IM or IV. This can be repeated one hour after the initial dose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nurses-responsibility-in-the-administration-of-bz">Nurses responsibility in the administration of BZ<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurses-responsibility-in-the-administration-of-bz" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Administer with food to minimize gastric irritation.</li>
<li>Advise the patient to take medication as exactly as directed. Abrupt withdrawal may cause insomnia, irritability and sometimes even seizures.</li>
<li>Explain about adverse effects and advise him to avoid activities that require alertness.</li>
<li>Caution the patient to avoid alcohol or any other CNS depressants along</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-antiparkinsonian-drugs">D. Antiparkinsonian Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-antiparkinsonian-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are drugs given to counteract the side effects of major tranquilizers. They are used as treatment for medication induced movement disorders, particularly neuroleptic – induced Parkinsonism, acute dystonia and medication induced tremors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="anticholinergics">Anticholinergics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anticholinergics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Trihexyphenidyl (Artane, trihexane, Trihexy, Pacitane)</li>
<li>Benztropine (Cogentin) whose initial dose is 0.1-1mg daily, the maintenance dose is 0.5-6mg daily divided into two or four times.</li>
<li>Biperaden</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="dopaminergic-agents">Dopaminergic agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dopaminergic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Bromocriptine</li>
<li>Carbidopa / levodopa.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="artane">Artane<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#artane" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Drug – induced Parkinsonism.</li>
<li>Adjunct in the management of Parkinsonism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="moa">MOA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Increases the release of dopamine. Usually given 1-2 mg per day orally initially, maximum dose up to 15mg/day in divided doses.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dizziness, nervousness, drowsiness, weakness, headache, confusion, blurred vision, mydriasis, tachycardia, orthostatic hypotension, dry mouth, nausea, constipation, vomiting, urinary retention and decreased sweating.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="831edf6b">Nurse’s responsibility<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#831edf6b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Assess parkinsonian and extrapyramidal symptoms. Medications should be tapered gradually.
Caution: patient to make position changes slowly to minimize orthostatic hypotension.
Instruct the patient about frequent rinsing of the mouth and good oral hygiene.
Caution: patient that this medication decreases perspiration and overheating may occur during hot weather.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antabuse-drugs">ANTABUSE DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antabuse-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disulfiram is an important drug in this class and is used to ensure abstinence in the treatment of alcohol dependence. Its main effect is to produce a rapid and violently unpleasant reaction in a person who ingests even a small amount of alcohol while taking Disulfiram.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mood-stabilizers">MOOD STABILIZERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood-stabilizers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lithium which is available in the following preparations:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lithium carbonate: 300mg tablets; 400mg tablets.</li>
<li>Lithium citrate: 300mg/5ml liquid.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The usual range of dose per day in acute mania is 900-2100 mg given in 2-3 divided doses.</p>
<p>Carbamazepine (Tegretol, Mazetol, Zeptol and Zen Retard). The average daily dose is 600-1800 mg orally in divided doses.</p>
<p>Sodium Valproate (Encoratechrono, Valparin, Epilex, Epival). The usual dose is 15mg/kg/day with a maximum of 60mg/kg/day orally.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-psychological-treatments">B. Psychological Treatments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-psychological-treatments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Having completed your look at the physical treatment methods, you will now look at some of the psychological treatments used to treat patients suffering from mental health illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-psychotherapy">I. Psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a form of treatment involving communication between the patient and the therapist, with the aim of modifying and alleviating illness. Employs verbal communication as the means of treatment aimed at relieving the patient's symptoms and helping him to understand and modify his conduct so as to lead a well-adjusted life.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-psychotherapy">Types of psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Dimension</th><th>Types</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Depending on the number of patients taking part</td><td>Individual psychotherapy</td></tr><tr><td>Group psychotherapy</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Depending on the duration of treatment</td><td>Long term psychotherapy</td></tr><tr><td>Short term psychotherapy</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Depending on the amount of responsibility given to the patient</td><td>Supportive</td></tr><tr><td>Deep</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Depending on the nature of the group</td><td>Family</td></tr><tr><td>Marital</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Group</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Therapy with children &amp; adolescents</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="individual-psychotherapy">Individual psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#individual-psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is a method of bringing about change in a person by exploring his or her feelings, attitudes, thinking and behaviour. Therapy is conducted on a one-to-one basis, i.e. the therapist treats one patient at a time. Patients generally seek this kind of therapy based on their desire. Such therapy helps to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Understand themselves and their behaviour.</li>
<li>Make personal changes.</li>
<li>Improve interpersonal relationships.</li>
<li>Get relief from emotional pain or unhappiness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Stress – related disorders</li>
<li>Alcohol and drug dependence</li>
<li>Sexual disorders</li>
<li>Marital disharmony</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="therapy-process">Therapy process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapy-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The patient is encouraged to discover for himself the reasons for his behaviour.</p>
<p>The therapist listens to the patient and offers explanation and advise when necessary.</p>
<p>By this he helps the patient to come to a greater understanding of self and to find a way of dealing with his problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="approaches">Approaches<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#approaches" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are four main approaches to individual therapy which includes:</p>
<ol>
<li>Psychodynamic therapy</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>

<p>Based on the assumption that when a patient has insight into early relationships and experiences as the source of his or her problems they can be resolved.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-humanistic-therapy">2. Humanistic therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-humanistic-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Centers on the patients view of the world and his or her problems.</p>
<p>The goal is to help patients realize their full potential through the therapist's genuineness, unconditional positive regard, which fosters the patient's sense of self-worth and empathetic understanding of the patient's point of view. This therapy is non-directive but focuses on helping the patient to explore and clarify his or her own feelings and choices.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-behaviour-therapy">3. Behaviour Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-behaviour-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is defined as a therapeutic technique, which attempts to change the patient's behaviour directly rather than correct the basic cause of the undesirable behaviour.</p>
<p>The two main methods that are used are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Changing the behaviour from inside using covert and cognitive therapies. Here, the priority is to help the patient modify their view of the world and themselves, by helping them change the things they say about themselves.</li>
<li>Changing the behaviour from outside. This is achieved through positive reinforcement of acceptable behaviour and negative reinforcement for unacceptable behaviour.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-cognitive-therapy">4. Cognitive therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-cognitive-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Based on the idea that behavior is secondary to thinking. It focuses on how patients think about themselves and their world, make changes in their current ways of thinking and behaviour.</p>
<p>Focuses on identifying and correcting distorted thinking patterns that can lead to emotional distress and problem behaviours.</p>
<p>This therapy is based on the belief that patients are the architects of their own misfortune and have control over their own thoughts and actions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="techniques-of-cognitive-therapy">Techniques of cognitive therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#techniques-of-cognitive-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are 4 main groups of cognitive techniques. They are the following:</p>
<p>a. Techniques for stopping intrusive cognitions</p>
<p>These methods aim at stopping intruding thoughts through distraction.</p>
<p>Attention is directed to another mental act like doing mental arithmetic or copying a figure.</p>
<p>b. Techniques to counterbalance faulty cognitions</p>
<p>This involves counterbalancing intruding cognitions and the emotions provoked by them, with another thought.</p>
<p>As an example, when an anxious patient with chest pain becomes apprehensive thinking he has a "heart problem", he may be trained to think that it is only a muscular pain and does not relate to the heart.</p>
<p>c. Techniques for altering cognitions</p>
<p>These are aimed at changing the nature of cognitions. The patient is helped to identify "maladaptive cognitions" and their "logical errors". Some errors are not mutually exclusive and which occur in depression are given below:</p>
<ul>
<li>Faulty inference: this is making faulty interpretations of a situation or an event where there is no factual evidence to make such conclusions. For example, if a friend fails to respond to a letter sent by the patient, he considers it as a sign of the friend's hostility or dislike to the latter.</li>
<li>Overgeneralization: this is making a general conclusion based on a single incident. An example is generalizing all students of a particular class as substandard, based on the poor marks scored by one student.</li>
<li>Magnification or minimization: these are distorted evaluations. For example a minor error is magnified or an important achievement is minimized in an unrealistically distorted manner.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unrealistic-assumptions">Unrealistic assumptions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unrealistic-assumptions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An example is the assumption one can be happy only if one is a top scorer all the time.</p>
<p>d. Techniques to resolve problems directly</p>
<p>These involve several steps and consists of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Defining the problem more clearly.</li>
<li>Dividing it small sub problem which can be better managed.</li>
<li>Finding out alternative methods of solving each subproblem.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Considering the merits and demerits of each method.
Selecting one method which is most advantageous at that instance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-supportive-psychotherapy">II. Supportive psychotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-supportive-psychotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this the therapist helps the patient to relieve emotional distress and symptoms without probing into the past and changing the personality. He uses various techniques such as:</p>
<p>Ventilation: It is a free expression of feelings or emotions. Patient is encouraged to talk freely whatever comes to his mind.</p>
<p>Environmental modification:/manipulation: Improving the well-being of mental patients by changing their living condition.</p>
<p>Persuasion: Here the therapist attempts to modify the patient’s behaviour by reasoning.</p>
<p>Re-education: Education to the patient regarding his problems, ways of coping, etc.</p>
<p>Reassurance: Reassurance is used to dispel apprehension and to restore confidence and promote hope. However care should be taken against offering false reassurance and providing it prematurely even before the patient has fully opened up.</p>
<p>Explanation: The explanation of the nature of symptoms and their causes is done by the therapist during the therapy. The choice of treatment and the likely outcome are explained to the patient.</p>
<p>Guidance: Guidance involves offering direct advice on handling particularly difficult situations in the real life of the patient. He may be advised on how and when he should seek help in the future. Suggestion involves advising in an indirect manner.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phases-of-therapy">Phases of therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phases-of-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Initial phase: Focused on assessment and relationship formation. Assessment encompasses full physical and psychiatric evaluation including level of motivation, the patient’s strengths and weaknesses. The therapist should be able to empathize with the patient in order to understand him better.</p>
<p>The working phase: Involves intense therapeutic activity and there is further exploration of the patient’s problems and life situations. The various therapeutic techniques are applied and attempts are made to give the patient an insight into his problems.</p>
<p>The terminal phase: Is intended to strengthen the patient’s improvement and to prepare him to end his treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iii-psychoanalytic-therapy">III. Psychoanalytic therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iii-psychoanalytic-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="assignment-read-on-psychoanalytic-theory-by-sigmund-freud">Assignment: read on psychoanalytic theory by Sigmund Freud<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment-read-on-psychoanalytic-theory-by-sigmund-freud" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The main indication is the presence of long standing mental conflicts, which may be unconscious but produce symptoms. In psychoanalysis the focus is on the cause of the problem, which is buried somewhere in the unconscious. The therapist tries to take the patient in the past in an effort to determine where the problem began. The aim of the therapy is to bring all the repressed material to conscious awareness so that the patient can work towards a healthy resolution of his problems, which are causing the symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="therapy-process">Therapy process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapy-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The psychoanalyst typically is positioned at the head of the patient and slightly behind, so that the patient cannot see the therapist. This decreases any kind of non-verbal communication between the two people. The patient is typically on the couch, relaxed, and ready to focus on the therapist’s instruction, which facilitates free association. The patient is an active participant, freely revealing all thoughts exactly as they occur and describing all dreams. The psychoanalyst is a shadow person. He reveals nothing personal, nor does he give any directions to the patient.</p>
<p>His verbal responses are for the most part brief and non-committal, so as not to interfere with the associative flow.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>0</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Some of the techniques used in psychoanalysis are:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="free-association">Free association<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#free-association" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient is allowed to speak whatever comes to his mind, in response to a word that is given by the therapist. For example, the therapist might say “mother” or “blue” and the patient would give a response, also typically one word, to each of the word the therapist says.</p>
<p>The therapist then looks for a theme or pattern to the patient’s responses. So if the patient responds “evil” to the word “mother” or “dead” to the word “blue” the therapist might pick up one potential theme, but if the patient responds “kind” and “true” to the words “mother” and “blue” respectively, the therapist might hear a completely different theme. The theme may give the therapist an idea of the cause of the patient’s emotional disturbance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dream-analysis">Dream analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dream-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Freud believed that behaviour is rooted in the unconscious and that dreams are a manifestation of the troubles people repress, the better way to get an idea of the problem is to monitor and interpret dreams.</p>
<p>The patient is asked to keep a dream lag. Analysis of the patient’s dreams helps to gain additional insight into his problem and the resistances. Thus dreams symbolically communicate areas of intrapsychic conflicts through the use of interpretation.</p>
<p>The process is complicated by the occurrence of transference reactions. This refers to the patient’s development of strong positive or negative feelings towards the analyst, and they represent the patient’s past response to a significant other, usually a parent. The patient’s reciprocal response to the patient is called countertransference. Such reactions must be handled appropriately before the progress can be made.</p>
<p>By termination of therapy, the patient is able to conduct his life according to an accurate assessment of external reality and is also able to relate to others uninhibited by neurotic conflicts.</p>
<p>Psychoanalytical therapy is a long term proposition. The patient is seen frequently, usually 5 times a week. It is therefore time consuming and expensive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypnosis">Hypnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an artificially induced state in which the person is relaxed and usually suggestible. The relaxation is guided by a therapist.</p>
<p>Hypnosis is also a means for entering an altered state of consciousness and in this state using visualization and suggestion to bring about desired changes in behaviour and thinking.</p>
<p>Can be induced in many ways such as by using a fixed point for attention, rhythmic monotonous instructions etc.</p>
<p>In hypnotherapy relaxation is guided by the therapist who has been trained in techniques of trance formation and who then asks certain questions of the patient or uses guided imagery to help picture the situation in an effort to find the cause of the problem.</p>
<p>At the end of the session, the therapist leaves some helpful hints for the patients.</p>
<p>These are called posthypnotic suggestions and typically include positive affirming statements for the patient to think about as well as instructions to help the patient accomplish self-hypnosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="catharsis">Catharsis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#catharsis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the act of purging or purification or elimination of a complex by bringing it to consciousness and affording to expression.</p>
<p>In psychoanalysis the therapist helps the person see the root of the problem and then, by talking or some other means, allows the patient to learn to evacuate this problem from the psyche. This can take place in conjunction with other form of psychoanalysis.</p>
<p>These therapies are undertaken on a one-to-one basis between the patient and the therapist. The nurse can be helpful in the treatment process by allowing the patient to talk about experiences in therapy and by carefully documenting the responses of the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="abreaction-therapy">Abreaction therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abreaction-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This is a process by which repressed material, particularly a painful experience or conflict is brought back to consciousness. The person not only recalls but also relieves the material, which is accompanied by the appropriate emotional response.</p>
<p>It is most useful in acute neurotic conditions caused by extreme stress (PTSD, hysteria etc)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This can be brought about by strong encouragement to relieve the stressful events. The procedure is begun with neutral topics at first, and gradually approaches areas of conflict.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iv-family-and-marital-therapy">IV. Family and marital therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iv-family-and-marital-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is that branch of psychiatry which sees an individual’s psychiatric symptoms as inseparably related to the family in which he lives. Therefore the focus of the treatment is not the individual but the family.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Whenever there is relational problems within a family or marital unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-therapy">Components of therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Assessment of family structure, roles, boundaries, resources, communication patterns and problem solving skills.</li>
<li>Teaching communication skills.</li>
<li>Teaching problem solving skills.</li>
<li>Writing a behavioural marital contract.</li>
<li>Homework assignments.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-family-therapy">Types of family therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-family-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="individual-family-therapy">Individual family therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#individual-family-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Each family member has a single therapist. The whole family may meet occasionally with one or two of the therapists to see how the members are relating to one another and work out specific issues that have been defined by individual members.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="conjoint-family-therapy">Conjoint family therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conjoint-family-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The nuclear family is seen, and the issues and problems raised by the family are the ones addressed by the therapist. The way in which the family interacts is observed and becomes the focus of therapy.</p>
<p>The therapist helps the family deal more effectively with problems as they arise and are defined.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="couples-therapy">Couples therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#couples-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Couples are often seen by the therapist together.</p>
<p>The couple may be experiencing difficulties in their marriage, and in therapy they are helped to work together to seek a resolution for their problems.</p>
<p>Family patterns, interaction and communication styles, and each partner’s goals, hopes and expectations are examined in therapy.</p>
<p>This examination enables the couple to find a common ground for resolving conflicts by recognizing and respecting each other’s similarities and differences.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="multiple-family-group-therapy">Multiple family group therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#multiple-family-group-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>4 or 5 families meet weekly to confront and deal with problems or issues they have in common.</p>
<p>Ability or inability to function well in the home and community, fear of talking to or relating to others, abuse, anger, neglect, the development of social skills, and responsibility for oneself are some of the issues on which these groups focus.</p>
<p>The multiple family group becomes the support for all the families.</p>
<p>The network also encourages each person to reach out and form new relationships outside the group.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="v-group-therapy">V. GROUP THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#v-group-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a treatment in which carefully selected people who are emotionally ill meet in a group guided by a trained therapist, and help one another effect personality change.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>0</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="selection">Selection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#selection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Homogeneous groups</li>
<li>Adolescents and patients with personality disorders.</li>
<li>Families and couples where the system needs change.</li>
<li>Contraindications</li>
<li>Antisocial patients</li>
<li>Actively suicidal or severely depressed patients.</li>
<li>Patients who are delusional and who may incorporate the group into their delusional system.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="group-size">Group size<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group-size" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Optimal size is 8-10 members. Sessions conducted once a week; each session may last for 45 minutes to one hour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="approaches-to-group-therapy">Approaches to group therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#approaches-to-group-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The therapist role is primarily that of a facilitator; he should provide a safe, comfortable atmosphere for self-disclosure.</li>
<li>Focus on the ‘here’ and ‘now’.</li>
<li>Use any transference situations to develop insight into their problems.</li>
<li>Protect members from verbal abuse or from scapegoating.</li>
<li>Whenever appropriate, provide positive reinforcement, this gives ego support and encourage future growth.</li>
<li>Handle circumstantial patients, hallucinating and delusional patients in a manner that protects the self-esteem of the individual and also sets limit on the behaviour so as to protect other group members.</li>
<li>Develop ability to recognize when a group member is fragile; he should be approached in a gentle, supportive and non-threatening manner.</li>
<li>Use silence effectively to encourage introspection and facilitate insight.</li>
<li>Laughter and a moderate amount of joking can act as a safety valve and at times contribute to group cohesiveness.</li>
<li>Role playing may help a member develop insight into the ways in which he relates to others.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="therapeutic-factors-involved-in-group-therapy">Therapeutic factors involved in group therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-factors-involved-in-group-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Sharing experience:</strong> This helps the patients to realize that they are not isolated and that others have similar experiences and problems.</p>
<p>Hearing from other patients that they have shared experiences is often more convincing and helpful than reassurance from the therapist.</p>
<p><strong>Support to and from group members:</strong> receiving help from other group members can be supportive to the person helped. The sharing action of being mutually supportive is an aspect of the group cohesiveness that can provide a sense of belonging for patients who feel isolated in their everyday lives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="socialization">Socialization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#socialization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is acquisition of social skills e.g. maintaining eye contact within a group through comments that members provide about one another’s deficiencies in social skills. This process can be helped by trying out new ways of interacting within the safety of the group.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="imitation">Imitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#imitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is learning from observing and adopting the behaviours of other group members. If the group is run well, patients imitate the adaptive behaviours of other group members.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="interpersonal-learning">Interpersonal learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interpersonal-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It refers to learning about difficulties in relationships by examining the interaction of individuals with the other members of the group.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="some-techniques-useful-in-group-therapy">Some techniques useful in group therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#some-techniques-useful-in-group-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Reflecting or rewarding comments of group members.</li>
</ul>
<p>30 | Page</p>
<ul>
<li>Asking for group reaction to one member’s statement.</li>
<li>Asking for individual reaction to one member’s statement.</li>
<li>Pointing out any shared feelings within the group.</li>
<li>Summarizing various points at the end of the session.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vi-behaviour-therapy">VI. BEHAVIOUR THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vi-behaviour-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a form of treatment for problems in which a trained person deliberately establishes a professional relationship with the patient, with the objective of removing or modifying existing symptoms and promoting positive personality, growth and development.</p>
<p>Involves identifying maladaptive behaviours and seeking to correct these by applying the principles of learning derived from the following theories:</p>
<p><strong>Assignment read on the following</strong></p>
<p>Classical conditioning model by Ivan Pavlov (1936)</p>
<p>Operant conditioning model by BF Skinner (1953)</p>
<p><strong>Major assumptions of behaviour therapy</strong></p>
<p>Based on the above mentioned theories, the following are the assumptions of BT:</p>
<p><strong>All behaviour is learned (adaptive and maladaptive)</strong></p>
<p>Human beings are passive organisms that can be conditioned or shaped to do anything if correct responses are rewarded or reinforced.</p>
<p>Maladaptive behaviour can be unlearned and replaced by adaptive behaviour if the person receives exposure to specific stimuli and reinforcement for the desired adaptive behaviour.</p>
<p>Behavioural assessment is focused more on the current behaviour rather than historical antecedents.</p>
<p>BT is a short duration therapy, therapists are easy to train and it is cost effective.</p>
<p>The total duration of therapy is usually 6-8 weeks.</p>
<p>Initial sessions are given daily but the later sessions are spaced out.</p>
<p>Unlike psychoanalysis where the therapist is a shadow person, in behaviour therapy both the patient and the therapist are equal participants.</p>
<p>There is no attempt to unearth an underlying conflict and the patient is not encouraged to explore his past.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="behaviour-techniques">Behaviour techniques<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#behaviour-techniques" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li><strong>Systematic desensitization</strong>: it was developed by Joseph Wolpe, based on the behavioral principle of counter conditioning. In this patients attain a state of complete relaxation and are then exposed to the stimulus that elicits the anxiety response. The negative reaction of anxiety is inhibited by the relaxed state, a process called reciprocal inhibition. It consists of 3 main steps:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Relaxation training.</li>
<li>Hierarchy construction.</li>
<li>Desensitization of the stimulus.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Relaxation training</strong>: there are many methods which can be used to induce relaxation. Some of them are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Jacobson’s progressive muscle relaxation</li>
<li>Hypnosis</li>
<li>Meditation or yoga</li>
<li>Mental imagery</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Hierarchy construction</strong>: Here the patient is asked to list all the conditions which provoke anxiety. Then he is asked to list them in descending disorder of anxiety provocation.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>31 | Page</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Desensitization of the stimulus: This can either be done in reality or through imagination. At first, the lowest item in hierarchy is confronted. The patient is advised to signal whenever anxiety is produced. With each signal he is asked to relax. After a few trials, patient is able to control his anxiety gradually.</p>
<p>Indications: phobias, obsessions, compulsions, certain sexual disorders.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Flooding: The patient is directly exposed to the phobic stimulus, but escape is made impossible.</li>
</ol>
<p>By prolonged contact with the phobic stimulus, the therapist's guidance and encouragement and his modeling behaviour reduce anxiety.</p>
<p>Indication: phobias</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Aversion therapy: Pairing of the pleasant stimuli with an unpleasant response, so that even in absence of the unpleasant response the pleasant stimulus becomes unpleasant by association.</li>
</ol>
<p>Punishment is presented immediately after a specific behavioural response and the response is eventually inhibited.</p>
<p>Unpleasant response is produced by electric stimulus, drugs, social disapproval or even fantasy.</p>
<p>Indications: Alcohol abuse, paraphilias, homosexuality, transvetism.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Operant conditioning procedures for increasing adaptive behaviour</li>
</ol>
<p>Positive reinforcement: when a behavioural response is followed by a generally rewarding event such as food, praise or gifts, it tends to be strengthened and occurs more frequently than before the reward. This technique is used to increase desired behaviour.</p>
<p>Token economy: this program involves giving token rewards for appropriate or desired targets. For example, in inpatient hospital wards, patients receive a reward for performing a desires behavior, such as tokens which they may use to purchase luxury items or certain privileges.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Operant conditioning procedures to teach new behaviour</li>
</ol>
<p>Modeling: This is a method of teaching by demonstration, where in the therapist shows how a specific behaviour is to be performed. In modeling the patient observes other patients indulging into the Internet, the therapist starts shaping by reinforcing the existing behaviour. Once it is established he reinforces the responses which are closest to the desired behaviour, and ignores the other responses.</p>
<p>For example, to establish eye to eye contact, the therapist sits opposite the patient and reinforces him even if he moves his upper body towards him. Once this is established, he reinforces the person's head movement in his direction and this procedure continues till eye to eye contact is established.</p>
<p>Chaining: this is used when a person fails to perform a complex task. The complex task is broken into a number of small steps and each step is taught to the patient. In forward chaining one starts with the first step, then to the third and so on. In backward chaining, one starts with the last step and goes on to the next step in a backward fashion.</p>
<ol start="6">
