<li>Operant conditioning procedures for decreasing maladaptive behaviour</li>
</ol>
<p>Extinction/Ignoring: Means removal of attention rewards permanently, following a problem behaviour. This includes actions like not looking at the patient, not talking to the patient or having no physical contact with the patient, etc. following the problem behaviour. This is commonly used when the patient exhibits odd behaviour.</p>
<p>Punishment: punishment is presented contingent upon the undesirable response. The punishment procedure should be administered immediately and consistently following the undesirable behaviour with clear explanation.</p>
<p>Timeout: this method includes removing the patient from the reward or the reward from the patient for a particular period of time following problem behaviour. This is often used in the treatment of childhood disorders.</p>
<p>Restitution (over-correction): this means restoring the disturbed situation to a state that is much better than what it was before the occurrence of the problem behaviour. For example, if a patient passes urine in the ward he would be required to not only clean the dirty area but also mop the entire area of the floor in the ward.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Response cost: this procedure is used with individuals who are on token programs for teaching adaptive behaviour. When undesirable behaviour occurs, a fixed number of tokens or points are deducted from what the individual has already earned.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-assertiveness-and-social-skill-training">7. Assertiveness and social skill training:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-assertiveness-and-social-skill-training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a BT technique in which the patient is given training to bring about change in emotional and other behavioural pattern by being assertive. Patient is encouraged not to be afraid of showing appropriate response, negative or positive, to an idea or suggestion. Provided by the therapist, first by role play and then by practice in a real life situation. Attention is focused on more effective interpersonal skills. Helps to improve social manners like encouraging eye contact, speaking appropriately, observing simple etiquette, and relating to people.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vii-play-therapy">VII. PLAY THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vii-play-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Play is a natural mode of growth and development in children. Through play a child learns to express his expressions and it serves as a tool in the development of the child.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="curative-factors">Curative factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#curative-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>It releases tension and pent-up emotions.</li>
<li>It allows compensation for loss and failures.</li>
<li>It improves emotional growth through his relationship with other children.</li>
<li>It provides an opportunity to the child to act out his fantasies and conflicts, to get rid of aggression and to learn positive qualities from other children.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="diagnostic-functions">Diagnostic functions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Play therapy gives the therapist a chance to explore family relationships of the child and discover what difficulties are contributing to the child’s problems.</li>
<li>Play therapy allows studying hidden aspects of the child’s personality.</li>
<li>It is possible to obtain a good idea of the intelligence level of the child.</li>
<li>Through play inter-sibling relationships can be adequately studied.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-play-therapy">Types of play therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-play-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Individual vs. group play therapy</strong>: In individual therapy the child is allowed to play by himself and the therapist attention is focused on this one child alone. In group play therapy other children are involved.</p>
<p><strong>Free play vs. controlled play therapy</strong>: In free play the child is given freedom deciding with what toys he wants to play with. In controlled play therapy, the child is introduced into a scene where the situation or setting is already established.</p>
<p><strong>Structured vs. unstructured play therapy</strong>: SPT involves organizing the situation in such a way so as to obtain more information. In USPT no situation is set and no plans are followed.</p>
<p><strong>Directive vs. non-directive play therapy</strong>: In DPT, the therapist totally sets directions, whereas in NDPT, the child receives no directions.</p>
<ul>
<li>Play therapy is generally conducted in a play room. The playroom should be suitably stocked with adequate play material, depending upon the problems of the child.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="viii-psychodrama">VIII. PSYCHODRAMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#viii-psychodrama" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a specialized type of group therapy that employs a dramatic approach in which the patient becomes actors in life situation scenarios. The goal is to resolve interpersonal conflicts in a less threatening atmosphere than the real life situation would present.</p>
<p>The patient is brought directly into the situation as an active participant. The director co-ordinates the process so that the group and the protagonist receive maximal benefit. Other group members act as auxiliary egos and play the roles of significant others with whom relationships are being explored.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>33 | Page</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The primary advantage of psychodrama is its direct access to re-enacting painful situations so that the painful emotions associated with them can be reworked, with the potential for spontaneously learning new responses in a safe therapeutic environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ix-music-therapy">IX. MUSIC THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ix-music-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the functional application of music towards the attainment of specific therapeutic goals.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Facilitates emotional expressions.</li>
<li>Improves cognitive skills like learning listening and attention span.</li>
<li>Social interaction is stimulated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="x-dance-therapy">X. DANCE THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#x-dance-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is psychotherapeutic use of movement, which furthers the emotional and physical integration of the individual.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Helps to develop body awareness.</li>
<li>Facilitates expression of feelings.</li>
<li>Improves interaction and communication.</li>
<li>Fosters integration of physical, emotional and social experiences that result in a sense of increased self-confidence and contentment.</li>
<li>Exercise through body movement maintains good circulation and muscle tone.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="xi-recretional-therapy">XI. RECRETIONAL THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#xi-recretional-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a form of activity therapy used in most psychiatric settings. It is a planned therapeutic activity that enables people with limitations to engage in recreational experiences.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aims">Aims<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>To encourage social interaction.</li>
<li>To decrease withdrawal tendencies.</li>
<li>To provide outlet for feelings.</li>
<li>To promote socially acceptable behaviour.</li>
<li>To develop skills, talents and abilities.</li>
<li>To increase physical confidence and a feeling of self-worth.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="points-to-be-kept-in-mind">Points to be kept in mind<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-be-kept-in-mind" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide a non-threatening and non-demanding environment.</li>
<li>Provide activities that are relaxing and without rigid guidelines and time-frames.</li>
<li>Provides activities that are enjoyable and self-satisfying.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-recreational-activities">Types of recreational activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-recreational-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Motor forms:</strong> These can further be divided into fundamental and accessory; among the fundamental forms are such games as hockey and football, while accessory forms are exemplified by play activity and dancing.</p>
<p><strong>Sensory forms:</strong> These can either be visual, for example looking at motion pictures, play etc or auditory such as listening to a concert.</p>
<p><strong>Intellectual forms:</strong> These include reading, debating and so on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="xii-relaxation-therapies">XII. RELAXATION THERAPIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#xii-relaxation-therapies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Relaxation produces physiological effects opposite those of anxiety: this includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Slowed heartrate,</li>
<li>Increased peripheral blood flow and neuromuscular stability.</li>
</ul>
<p>There are many methods which can be used to induce relaxation.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This document is available on
35 | Page</p>
<p>a. Progressive muscular relaxation</p>
<p>It is a method of deep-muscle relaxation which is based on the premise that the body responds to anxiety provoking thoughts and events with muscle tension.</p>
<p>Indications</p>
<p>Muscular tension    Muscle spasms
Anxiety             Neck and back pain
Insomnia            High blood pressure
Depression           Mild phobia
Fatigue            Stuttering
Irritable bowel</p>
<p>Technique</p>
<p>In this procedure the patient relaxes major muscle groups of the feet and working towards the head and vice versa.
Muscle relaxation can be done in sitting or lying down position.
Each muscle group is tensed for 5 – 7 seconds and then relaxed for 20 to 30 seconds, during which time the individual concentrates on the difference in sensations between the two conditions.
Soft slow background music may facilitate relaxation.</p>
<p>b. Mental imagery</p>
<p>It is a relaxation method in which patients are instructed to imagine themselves in a place associated with pleasant relaxed memories.
Such images allow patients to enter a relaxed state or experience a feeling of calmness and tranquility.
The frame of reference is very personal, based on what each individual considers being a relaxing environment.
Some might select a scene at the sea shore; some might choose a mountain atmosphere.
Using guided imagery can promote a sense of wellbeing in patients and help them change their perceptions about their disease, treatment and healing ability.
Significant especially during a painful or stressful event.</p>
<p>c. Yoga</p>
<p>This is based on the principle of body-mind unity whereby a chronically restless or agitated mind will result in poor health and decreased mental clarity.
Yoga uses a combination of physical postures, breathing techniques and meditation to promote relaxation and enhance the flow of vital energy.
The yoga system advocates identification of the soul with its final aim being union with the supreme being. This is brought about by the following 8 steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>Self-control obtained by such devices as chastity, non-stealing, non-violence, truthfulness and avoidance of greed.</li>
<li>Religious observance through chanting hymns, austerity, purity and contentment.</li>
<li>Assumption of certain positions.</li>
<li>Regulation of breath, with controlled rhythmic exhalation, inhalation and temporary suspension of breathing.</li>
<li>Restraint of the senses.</li>
<li>Steadying of the mind, through fixation on some part of the body, such as the nose or navel.</li>
<li>Meditation on the true object of knowledge, the supreme spirit, to the exclusion of other things in life.</li>
<li>Profound contemplation with such complete absorption and detachment that there is insensitivity to heat and cold, pain and pleasure.</li>
</ol>
<p>d. Meditation</p>
<p>This is a kind of self-discipline that helps one achieve inner peace and harmony by focusing uncritically on one thing at a time.</p>
<p>Studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Medical meditation and Yoga balances and regenerates spiritual and physical energies, thus forging a healing alliance in which the spirit nurtures body and mind.</p>
<p>Mindful meditation refers to focusing on physical sensations, such as movement or breath, and on the thoughts in order to increase awareness and enhance living in the movement to the fullest extent possible.</p>
<p>It promotes deep states of psychological and physical relaxation.</p>
<p>Beneficial for patients with depression and anxiety.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="e-physical-exercise">e. Physical exercise<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-physical-exercise" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Regular exercise is the most effective method of relieving stress by providing a natural outlet for tension produced by the body in its state of arousal for “fight or flight”</p>
<p>Aerobic exercises strengthen cardiovascular system and increases body’s ability to use oxygen more efficiently.</p>
<p>Aerobic exercises includes: brisk walking, jogging; running; cycling; swimming and dancing. To achieve the benefit of exercises they must be performed regularly for at least 30 minutes per day.</p>
<p>Effective in reducing general anxiety and depression.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="f-deep-breathing-exercises">f. Deep breathing exercises<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f-deep-breathing-exercises" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tension is released when the lungs are allowed to breath in as much oxygen as possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Anxiety</li>
<li>Depression</li>
<li>Irritability</li>
<li>Muscular tension</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="technique">Technique<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#technique" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Sit or lie down comfortably, inhale slowly through the nose and exhale through the mouth.</p>
<p>While inhaling place one hand below the ribs.</p>
<p>Allow that hand to expand outward when inhaled, let that hand fall back to its original position when exhaled.</p>
<p>Exhalation should take twice as long as inhalation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="xiii-occupational-therapy">XIII. OCCUPATIONAL THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#xiii-occupational-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the application of goal oriented, purposeful activity in the assessment and treatment of individuals with psychological, physical or developmental disabilities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="goal">Goal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>To enable the patient to achieve a healthy balance of occupations through the development of skills that will allow him to function satisfactory to himself and others.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Helps to develop social skills and provide an outlet for self-expression.</li>
<li>Strengthens ego defenses.</li>
<li>Develops a more realistic view of the self in relation to others.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="points-to-be-kept-in-mind">Points to be kept in mind<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-be-kept-in-mind" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient should be involved as much as possible in selecting the activity.</li>
<li>Select an activity that interests or has the potential to interest him.</li>
<li>The activity should utilize the patient’s strengths and abilities.</li>
<li>The activity should be of short duration to foster a feeling of accomplishment.</li>
<li>If possible the selected activity should provide some new experience to the patient.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-activities">Types of activities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-activities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Diversional activities: These activities are used to divert one's thoughts from life stresses or to fill time. E.g. organized games.</p>
<p>Therapeutic activities: these activities are used to obtain a specific care plan or goal. E.g. basket making, carpentry.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-physical-therapies">C. PHYSICAL THERAPIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-physical-therapies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are treatment approaches that use physiologic or physical interventions to effect behavioural change. The most common is ECT.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="electroconvulsive-therapy">ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electroconvulsive-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the artificial induction of a grandma seizure through the application of electrical current to the brain. The stimulus is applied through electrodes that are placed either bilaterally in the fronto-temporal region, or unilaterally on the non-dominant side (right side of the head in a right handed individual).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="parameters-of-electrical-current-applied">Parameters of Electrical current applied<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parameters-of-electrical-current-applied" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Voltage – 70 – 120 volts.</li>
<li>Duration – 0.7 – 1.5 seconds</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-seizure-produced">Types of seizure produced<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-seizure-produced" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Grandmal seizure-tonic phase lasting for 10-15 seconds.</li>
<li>Clonic phase lasting for 30-60 seconds.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-ect">Types of ECT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Direct ECT</strong>: in this, ECT is given in the absence of anaesthesia and muscular relaxation.</p>
<p><strong>Modified ECT</strong>: here the ECT is modified by drug induced muscular relaxation and general anesthesia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="frequency-and-total-number-of-ect">Frequency and total number of ECT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frequency-and-total-number-of-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Frequency</strong>: 3 times per week or as indicated.</p>
<p><strong>Total number</strong>: 6 to 10; upto 25 times may be preferred as indicated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="application-of-electrodes">Application of electrodes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#application-of-electrodes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Bilateral ECT</strong>: Each electrode is placed 2.5-4 cm above the midpoint, on a line joining the tragus of the ear and the lateral canthus of the eye.</p>
<p><strong>Unilateral ECT</strong>: Electrodes are placed only on one side of the head, usually non-dominant side (right side of the head in a right handed individual).</p>
<p>This is safer, with much fewer side effects particularly those of memory impairment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="indications">Indications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Major depression</strong>: with suicidal risk, stupor, poor intake of food and fluids, melancholia with psychotic features, unsatisfactory response to drugs or where drugs are contraindicated or have serious side effects.</p>
<p><strong>Severe catatonia</strong>: with stupor, poor intake of food and fluids, unsatisfactory response to drug therapy, or when drugs are contraindicated or have serious side effects.</p>
<p><strong>Severe psychosis (schizophrenia or mania)</strong>: with risk of suicide, homicide or danger of physical assault, depressive features, unsatisfactory response to drug therapy or when drugs are contraindicated or have serious side effects.</p>
<p><strong>Organic mental disorders</strong>: organic mood disorders, organic psychosis.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contraindications">Contraindications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraindications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="absolute">Absolute<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#absolute" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Raised ICP</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relative">Relative<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral aneurysm</li>
<li>Cerebral hemorrhage</li>
<li>Brain tumor</li>
<li>Acute myocardial infarction</li>
<li>Congestive heart failure</li>
<li>Pneumonia or aortic aneurysm.</li>
<li>Retinal detachment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects-of-ect">Side effects of ECT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Memory impairment</li>
<li>Drowsiness, confusion and restlessness</li>
<li>Poor concentration/ anxiety</li>
<li>Headache, weakness/fatigue, backache, muscle aches.</li>
<li>Dryness of mouth, palpitations, nausea, vomiting.</li>
<li>Unsteady gait.</li>
<li>Tongue bite and incontinence.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-of-the-nurse">Role of the nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-the-nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pre-treatment-evaluation">Pre-treatment evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-treatment-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Detailed medical and psychiatric history including history of allergies.</li>
<li>Assessment of patient’s and families knowledge of indications, side-effects, therapeutic effects and risks associated with ECT.</li>
<li>Any informed consent should be taken. Allay any unfounded fears and anxieties regarding the procedure.</li>
<li>Assess baseline vital signs.</li>
<li>Patient should be on empty stomach for 6-8 hours prior to ECT.</li>
<li>Withhold night doses of drugs, which increases seizure threshold like diazepam, barbiturates and anticonvulsants.</li>
<li>Withhold oral medications in the morning.</li>
<li>Head shampooing in the morning since oil causes impedance of passage of electricity to brain.</li>
<li>Any jewellery, prosthesis, dentures, contact lens, metallic objects and tight clothing should be removed from the patient’s body.</li>
<li>Empty bladder and bowel just before ECT.</li>
<li>Administration of 0.6 mg atropine IM or SC 30 minutes before ECT, or IV just before ECT.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="intra-procedure-care">Intra-procedure care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intra-procedure-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Place the patient comfortably on the ECT table in supine position.</li>
<li>Stay with the patient to allay anxiety and fear.</li>
<li>Assist in administering the anesthetic agent.</li>
<li>Since muscle relaxant paralyzes all muscles including respiratory muscles, patent airway should be ensured and ventilator support should be started.</li>
<li>Mouth gag should be inserted to prevent possible tongue bite.</li>
<li>The place(s) of electrode placement should be cleaned with normal saline or 25% bicarbonate solution, or a conducting gel applied.</li>
<li>Monitor voltage, intensity and duration of electric stimulus given.</li>
<li>Monitor seizure activity using cuff method.</li>
<li>100% oxygen should be provided.</li>
<li>During seizure monitor vital signs, ECG, oxygen saturation, EEG, etc.</li>
<li>Record findings and medicines given in the patient’s chart.</li>
</ul>
<p>38 | Page</p>
<p>Post-procedure care</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor vital signs.</li>
<li>Continue oxygenation till spontaneous respiration starts.</li>
<li>Assess for post-ictal confusion and restlessness.</li>
<li>Take safety precautions to prevent injury (side-lying position and suctioning to prevent aspiration of secretions, use of side rails to prevent falls).</li>
<li>If there is severe post-ictal confusion and restlessness, IV diazepam may be administered.</li>
<li>Reorient the patient after recovery and stay with him until fully oriented.</li>
<li>Document any findings as relevant in the patient’s record.</li>
</ul>
<p>ADMISSION AND DISCHARGE PROCEDURES OF MENTALLY SICK PATIENTS</p>
<p>Mental Health Act (Cap 248) and Legal Application
The Mental Health Act is an act of parliament to amend and consolidate the law relating to the care of persons who are suffering from mental disorders, or mental sub-normality with mental disorder, for the custody of these persons, management of their properties, management and control of a mental hospital and for custodial purposes.</p>
<p>The act provides for the procedures to be followed for reception into a mental hospital. It also stipulates that no person shall be received or detained for treatment in a mental hospital, unless they have been received and detained under this act or under criminal procedure code.</p>
<p>Kenyan Board of Mental Health
The act also provides for the establishment of a board, that is, the Kenya board of mental health for the purposes of administering this act.</p>
<p>The members of the Kenya board of mental health include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chairman, who can be the Director of Medical Services (DMS) or the Deputy Director of Medical Services and is appointed by the minister</li>
<li>Psychiatrist (medical practitioner) appointed by the minister.</li>
<li>One clinical officer with training and experience in mental health care appointed by the minister.</li>
<li>One psychiatric nurse with experience in mental health care, appointed by the minister.</li>
<li>The commissioner of social services or their nominee appointed by the minister.</li>
<li>Director of education or their nominee appointed by the minister.</li>
<li>A representative from each province in Kenya, being resident in the provinces, appointed by the minister.</li>
<li>The board may co-opt any person whose skills, knowledge or experience may be useful. It may also establish a committee for better function and regulate its own procedure.</li>
</ul>
<p>The functions of the Board are under the control and direction of the minister for health.</p>
<p>They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>To coordinate mental health activities in Kenya.</li>
<li>To advise the government on the state of mental health and mental health care facilities in Kenya.</li>
<li>To inspect mental health care hospitals to ensure that they meet the prescribed standards.</li>
<li>To approve the establishment of mental health care hospitals.</li>
<li>To assist when necessary in the administration of mental health hospitals.</li>
<li>To receive and investigate any matters referred to it by a patient or relative of a patient concerning the treatment of the patient at a mental health hospital and, where necessary, to take or recommend to the minister any remedial action.</li>
<li>To advise the government on the care of the persons suffering from mental sub-normality without mental disorder.</li>
<li>To initiate and organize community or family based programs for the care of persons suffering from mental disorder, and to perform such other functions as may be placed upon it by this act or under the law.</li>
</ul>
<p>Sections of the Mental Health Act
Part V - Voluntary Patients (Section 10)</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)
39 | Page</p>
<p>Any person who has attained the apparent age of sixteen years, decrees to voluntarily submit themselves to treatment for mental disorder, and who makes to the ‘person in charge’ a written application in duplicate in the form prescribed, may be perceived as a voluntary patient into a mental hospital.</p>
<p>The person fills in a form MOH 613, in duplicate provided for in the first schedule to these regulations before admitting them to the institution as an in-patient. This indicates that the admission is at their own request.</p>
<p>Any person who has not attained the apparent age of sixteen years and whose parent or guardian desires to submit them for treatment for mental disorder, may, if the guardian or parent makes to the ‘person in charge’ of a mental institution, a written application in duplicate in the prescribed forms, be perceived as a voluntary patient. In such cases forms MOH 637 in duplicate should be filled and signed by the guardian or the parent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-vi-involuntary-patients-section-14-m-h-a">Part VI - Involuntary Patients (Section 14 M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-vi-involuntary-patients-section-14-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Involuntary patients are those who are incapable of expressing themselves as willing or unwilling to receive treatment. They require the forms MOH 614 to be filled in duplicate by the husband, wife or relative of the patient, indicating the reasons why they are applying for admission.</p>
<p>Any person applying on behalf of another person should state the reasons why a relative could not make the application and specify their connection with the patient.</p>
<p>The patient is admitted for a period of not more than six months. The ‘person in charge’ can prolong this period by six more months provided the total period does not exceed twelve months. An MOH 615 form should be filled by the doctor indicating why he thinks that the patient can benefit from the treatment. They should write down their own name, qualifications, date and then sign the forms.</p>
<p>Both the MOH 614 and MOH 615 forms must reach the hospital within 14 days of the date they were signed, otherwise they become invalid.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-vii-emergency-admissions-section-1b-m-h-a">Part VII - Emergency Admissions (Section 1b M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-vii-emergency-admissions-section-1b-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A police officer, chief or assistant chief can arrest any person who is found to be dangerous to themselves or others, and take them to a mental hospital for treatment within 24 hours or a reasonable time. The patient should be reviewed after 72 hours and can be discharged if found to be of sound mind. If found to be of unsound mind, the patient may be admitted for treatment as an involuntary patient. For the purposes of admission, the form MOH 638 must be filled in by the police officer or an administrative officer.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-viii-admission-and-discharge-of-members-of-the-armed-forces-section-17-m-h-a">Part VIII - Admission and Discharge of Members of the Armed Forces (Section 17 M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-viii-admission-and-discharge-of-members-of-the-armed-forces-section-17-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any member of the armed forces may be admitted into a mental hospital for observation, if a medical officer of the armed forces, by letter addressed to the ‘person in charge’, and certifies that:</p>
<p>The member of the armed forces has been examined within a period of 48 hours before issuing the letter.</p>
<p>For reasons recorded in the letter, the member of the armed forces is a proper person to be admitted to a mental hospital for observation and treatment.</p>
<p>A member of the armed forces may be admitted under section 17 for an initial period of 28 days from the date of admission, that period may be extended if, at or before the end of 28 days, two medical practitioners, one of whom shall be a psychiatrist, recommend the extension after re-examining the patient.</p>
<p>The said patient can be discharged if two medical practitioners, one of whom is a psychiatrist, by a letter addressed to the ‘person in charge’, certifying that they have examined the member of the armed forces within a period of 72 hours before issuing the letter.</p>
<p>Where any member of the armed forces suffers from mental illness whilst away from his armed forces unit and is under any circumstance, admitted into a mental hospital, the ‘person in charge’ shall inform the nearest armed forces unit directly, or through an administrative officer or gazetted police officer.</p>
<p>If a member of the armed forces is admitted to a mental hospital they cease to be a member of the armed forces, the ‘person in charge’ shall be informed of that fact and the patient shall be declared an involuntary patient under part VI (section 14) with effect from the date the information is received.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="part-ix-admission-of-a-patient-from-foreign-countries-section-18-m-h-a">Part IX - Admission of a Patient from Foreign Countries (Section 18 M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#part-ix-admission-of-a-patient-from-foreign-countries-section-18-m-h-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>According to this section of the act:</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>No person suffering from mental disorder shall be admitted into a mental hospital in Kenya from any state outside Kenya except under Part IX of M.H.A.</p>
<p>This part will not apply to individuals ordinarily resident in Kenya.</p>
<p>(Section 19 M.H.A) Where it is necessary to admit a person suffering from mental disorder from any foreign country into any mental hospital in Kenya for observation, the government or other relevant authority in that country shall apply in writing to the mental health board to approve the admission, no mental hospital shall receive a person suffering mental disorders from a foreign country without the board's written approval.</p>
<p>The application for the board's approval under subsection (I) shall indicate that the person whom it relates to has been legally detained in the foreign country for a period not exceeding two months under the law in that country, relating to the detention and treatment of persons suffering from mental disorder, and their admission into mental hospital in Kenya has been found necessary.</p>
<p>No person shall be admitted under this section unless they are accompanied by a warrant or other documents together with the board's approval under subsection (2) shall be sufficient authority for their conveyance to admission and treatment in the mental hospital to which the board's approval relates.</p>
<p>According to this section of the act:</p>
<p>On the admission of a person into a mental hospital under this section, not being a person transferred to the mental hospital under section 23, the 'person in charge' shall within 72 hours or such longer period as the board may approve (i) Examine the person or cause the person to be examined to determine the extent of the mental disorder and the nature of treatment and</p>
<p>(ii) Within that period forward to the Board a report on the findings, together with the warrant or other document from the foreign country concerned accompanying the patient/person.</p>
<p>A person shall not be detained in a mental hospital under this section for a period longer than two months from the date of admission to the mental hospital unless the board, on application in the prescribed forms by the 'person in charge', approves.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c180e939">Part X – Discharge and Transfer of Patients (Section 21 and 22 of M.H.A)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c180e939" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The 'person in charge' of a mental hospital may, by order in writing, and upon the recommendation of the medical practitioner in charge of any person's treatment in the mental hospital, recommend discharge and that person shall thereupon be discharged as having recovered from mental disorder, provided that:</p>
<p>An order shall not be made under this section for a person who is detained under criminal procedure Cap 75.</p>
<p>This section shall not prejudice the board's powers under section 15 of M.H.A.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-15-provides-that">Section 15 provides that:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-15-provides-that" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Where any person has been received into a mental hospital under part V and part VI (voluntary and involuntary mode of admission), the board may at any time order that the person shall be discharged or otherwise dealt with under this act.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-22-order-for-delivery-of-patient-into-care-of-relative-of-friend">Section 22: Order for delivery of patient into care of relative of friend.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-22-order-for-delivery-of-patient-into-care-of-relative-of-friend" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If any relative or friend of a person admitted into any mental hospital under this act desires to take the person into their custody and care, they may apply to the 'person in charge' who may, subject to subsection (2), order that the person be delivered into the custody and care of the relative or friend upon such terms and conditions to be complied with by the relative or friend.</p>
<p>In the exercise of their powers subsection (1) the person in charge shall consult with the medical practitioner in charge of the person's treatment in the mental hospital and the board on the relevant district mental health council, which is performing the board's functions under section 7, subsection (1).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="15032c4f">Part XIV – Offences under MHA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#15032c4f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-47">Section 47:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-47" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is an offence for a person other than medical practitioner to sign certificates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-48">Section 48:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-48" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any medical practitioner who knowingly, wilfully or recklessly certifies anything in a certificate made under this act, which they know to be untrue, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>41 | Page</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Section 49:
It is an offence for any person to assist the escape of any person suffering from mental disorder being conveyed to or from, or while under care and treatment in a mental hospital. It is also an offence to harbour any person suffering from mental disorder that they know have escaped from a mental hospital.</p>
<p>Section 50:
It is an offence for any person in charge of or any person employed at a mental hospital to unlawfully permit a patient to leave such a hospital.</p>
<p>Section 51:
Any person in charge of, or any person employed at a mental hospital that strikes, ill-treats, abuses or wilfully neglects any patient in the mental hospital, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<p>Section 52:
Any person who without the consent of a ‘person in charge’ gives, sells or barters any articles or commodities of any kind, to any patient in a mental hospital, whether inside or outside the grounds of the mental hospital, shall be guilty of an offence.</p>
<p>Section 53:
General Penalty: Any person who is guilty of an offence under this act, or who contravenes any of the provisions of this act or any regulations made under this act, shall where no other penalty is provided, be liable on conviction to a fine not exceeding Ksh 10,000. or to imprisonment not exceeding twelve months or both.</p>
<p>PSYCHIATRIC DISORDERS</p>
<p>SCHIZOPHRENIA
This is a psychotic condition characterized by a disturbance in thinking, emotions, volitions and faculties in the presence of clear consciousness, which usually leads to social withdrawal.</p>
<p>A CLINICAL OVERVIEW OF SCHIZOPHRENIA AND OTHER PSYCHOTIC DISORDERS
Schizophrenia</p>
<p>Clinical features
A disturbance that lasts for at least 6 months and includes at least 1 month of 2 or more active phase symptoms.</p>
<p>The symptoms include:
Delusions, hallucinations, disorganised speech, grossly disorganised or catatonic behaviour, negative symptoms.</p>
<p>Subtypes
Paranoid,
Disorganised,
Catatonic,
Undifferentiated,
Residual.</p>
<p>Schizophreniform disorder is characterised by:
A symptomatic presentation that is equivalent to schizophrenia except aduration of 1 to 6 months.</p>
<p>Schizoaffective disorder is a disturbance in which a mood episode and the active phase symptoms of schizophrenia occur together were precede or are followed by at least 2 weeks of delusions or hallucinations without prominent mood symptoms.</p>
<p>Delusional disorder at least 1 month of non-bizarre delusions without other active-phase symptoms of schizophrenia.</p>
<p>Brief psychotic disorder: A psychotic disturbance that lasts more than 1 day and remits by 1 month.</p>
<p>Shared psychotic disorder: A disturbance that develops in an individual who is influenced by someone else who has an established delusion with similar content.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Psychotic disorder due to a general medical condition: psychotic symptoms are judged to be a direct physiological consequence of a GMC.</p>
<p>Substance induced psychotic disorder: psychotic symptoms are judged to be a direct physiological consequence of a drug of abuse, a medication or toxin exposure.</p>
<p>There are several risk factors associated with the conditions. Schizophrenia is often witnessed in individuals with family members who have schizophrenia or in children who are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Highly individualistic in their thought processes.</li>
<li>Overtly independent and obedient.</li>
<li>Shy, withdrawn and loners.</li>
<li>Unmanageable, prone to destructive, aggressive behaviour.</li>
<li>Truant from school.</li>
<li>Sensitive to separation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neurotransmitters">NEUROTRANSMITTERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurotransmitters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There is a hyperactivity of dopaminergic systems.</li>
<li>Drugs that increase dopamine (e.g. Amphetamine and cocaine) aggravate or trigger schizo.</li>
<li>Epinephrine activity is increased in schizo, leading to increased sensitization.</li>
<li>There is decrease in Gamma Amino butyric Acid (GABA) activity resulting in hyperactivity of dopaminergic neurons.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-signs-and-symptoms">CLINICAL SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="general-considerations">General considerations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-considerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>MSE and history taking is important.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="reality-distortion">Reality distortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reality-distortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This leads to delusions and auditory hallucinations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disorganization">Disorganization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorganization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This manifests as thought disorder, inappropriate affect and bizarre behavior.</p>
<p>The formal thought disorder results in incoherent speech.</p>
<p>In severe cases words maybe so mixed up (word salad) making it difficult to understand.</p>
<p>Psychomotor poverty (negative symptoms) these include:
Abolition – lack of initiative, decreased spontaneous movement, poverty of speech and blunted or flattened affect (main ones) others are; poor grooming, anhedonia and social withdrawal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="major-diagnostic-criteria-for-schizo">Major diagnostic criteria for schizo<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#major-diagnostic-criteria-for-schizo" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A. One month or more of at-least two of the following symptoms
Delusions
Hallucinations
Disorganized speech
Grossly disorganized or catatonic behavior
Negative symptoms (decrease expression of emotions, poverty of speech, loss of interests and drive, tremendous inertia)</p>
<p>B. Social and occupational dysfunction
One or more areas affected (work, relationships, self-care)</p>
<p>C. Duration
Continuous symptoms and signs for greater or equal to 6 months. These 6 months must include:
At least one month of symptoms meeting criteria 1.
Various combinations of prodromal and residual symptoms exclude:
Schizoaffective and mood disorder.
Substance use or a medical condition</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu
