<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="subtypes-of-schizophrenia">SUBTYPES OF SCHIZOPHRENIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subtypes-of-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="paranoid-schizophrenia">Paranoid Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paranoid-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A type of schizo in which the following criteria are met:</p>
<ul>
<li>Preoccupation with one or more delusions or frequent auditory hallucinations.</li>
<li>None of the following is dominant: disorganized speech, disorganized or catatonic behavior, or flat or inappropriate affect.</li>
<li>This is a disorder characterized by delusions of persecution or grandeur.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disorganized-hebephrenic-schizophrenia">Disorganized(Hebephrenic) Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disorganized-hebephrenic-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A type of schizo in which the following criteria are met:</p>
<p>A. All of the following are prominent:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disorganized speech.</li>
<li>Disorganized behavior.</li>
<li>Flat or inappropriate affect.</li>
</ul>
<p>B. The criteria are not met for catatonic type.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="catatonic-schizophrenia">Catatonic Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#catatonic-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A type of schizo in which the clinical picture is dominated by at least two of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Motoric immobility AEB catalepsy including waxy flexibility or stupor.</li>
<li>Excessive motor activity (that is apparently purposeless and not influenced by external stimuli).</li>
<li>Extreme negativism (an apparently motiveless resistance to all instructions or maintenance of a rigid posture against attempts to be moved) or mutism peculiarities of voluntary movement AEB posturing (voluntary assumption of inappropriate or bizarre postures), stereotyped movements, prominent mannerisms or prominent grimacing echolalia or echopraxia.</li>
</ul>
<p>This is a disorder characterized by a stuporous state in which the person is mute, negative or complains in response to a request. The individual may be immobile, display waxy flexibility and may retain urine and faces.</p>
<p>It may alternatively be characterized by a highly excited state in which the person is abusive, aggressive, and hyperactive or agitated (catatonic excitement).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="undifferentiated-schizophrenia">Undifferentiated Schizophrenia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#undifferentiated-schizophrenia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A type in which symptoms that meet criteria A are present, but the criteria are not met for the paranoid, disorganized or catatonic type.</p>
<p>This disorder is also known as simple types.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="residual-type">Residual type<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#residual-type" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the type in which the following criteria are met:</p>
<ul>
<li>Absence of prominent delusions, hallucinations, disorganized speech and grossly disorganized or catatonic behaviour.</li>
<li>There is continuing evidence of the disturbance as indicated by the presence of negative symptoms or two or more symptoms listed in criteria A for schizophrenia, present in an attenuated form (e.g. odd beliefs, unusual perceptual experiences).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations">INVESTIGATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Perform P/E and laboratory tests to rule out other medical conditions including malaria, typhoid, HIV/AIDS and substance use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pharmacological: Give antipsychotics</li>
<li>Physical therapies: ECT</li>
<li>Psychological therapies: group therapy, behaviour therapy, social skills training, cognitive therapy, family therapy.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
45 | Page</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Schizophrenic patients in an acute episode of the illness are seldom able to make a significant contribution to their history.</li>
<li>Data may be obtained from family members, other people familiar with the patient and also from old records.</li>
<li>A nursing assessment includes information regarding any previous incidence of mental illness or psychotic episodes.</li>
<li>Observe behaviour pattern, posturing, psychomotor disturbance, hygiene.</li>
<li>Identify the type of disturbance the patient is experiencing.</li>
<li>Ask the patient about feelings while thought alterations are evident.</li>
<li>Note the affect and the emotional tone of the patient and whether they are appropriate in relation to the thought or present situation.</li>
<li>Assess for theme and content of delusional thinking. If the delusion is persecution oriented, assess the nature of the threat and risk for violence.</li>
<li>Assess speech patterns associated with the delusions.</li>
<li>Assess for ability to perform self-care activity, i.e. sleep pattern and interaction with other patients.</li>
<li>Determine any suicidal intent or recent attempts that may have been made.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnosis">Nursing diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Disturbed thought process, related to inability to trust, panic anxiety evidenced by delusional thinking, extreme suspiciousness of others.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: the patient will:</p>
<ul>
<li>Eliminate pattern of delusional thinking.</li>
<li>Demonstrate trust in others.</li>
<li>Demonstrate decreased anxiety levels.</li>
<li>Demonstrate improved reality orientation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ineffective health maintenance related to inability to trust, extreme suspiciousness evidenced by poor diet intake, inadequate food and fluid intake, difficulty in falling asleep.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: the patient will:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain adequate nutrition, hydration and elimination.</li>
<li>Maintain adequate sleep and rest.</li>
<li>Take medication as administered.</li>
</ul>
<p>Self-care deficit related to withdrawal, regression, panic anxiety, cognitive impairment, inability to trust evidenced by difficulty in carrying out tasks associated with hygiene, dressing, grooming, eating, sleeping and toileting.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: the patient will:</p>
<ul>
<li>Demonstrate increased interest in self-care.</li>
<li>Complete daily activities with minimum assistance.</li>
<li>Demonstrate adequate personal hygiene.</li>
</ul>
<p>Potential for violence, self-directed or at others related to command hallucinations evidenced by physical violence, destruction of objects in the environment or self-destructive behaviour.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: the patient will:</p>
<ul>
<li>Not injure others or destroy property or self.</li>
<li>Verbalize feelings of anger or frustration.</li>
<li>Express decreased feeling of agitation fear or anxiety.</li>
<li>Risk for self-inflicted or life-threatening injury related to command hallucinations evidenced by suicidal ideas, plans or attempts.</li>
</ul>
<p>Goal/outcome: the patient will not harm him/herself.</p>
<p>Disturbed sensory perception (auditory/visual) related to panic anxiety or biochemical factors evidenced by inappropriate responses, disordered thought sequencing, poor concentration, disorientation, withdrawn behaviour.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: the patient will:</p>
<ul>
<li>Demonstrate decreased hallucinations.</li>
<li>Interact with others.</li>
<li>Verbalize plans to deal with hallucinations, if they recur.</li>
</ul>
<p>Social isolation related to inability to trust, panic anxiety, delusional thinking evidenced by withdrawal, sad, dull affect preoccupation with own thoughts, expression of feelings of rejection of aloneness imposed by others.</p>
<p>Goal/objective: patient will voluntarily spend time with other patients and staff members in group activities in the unit.</p>
<p>Impaired verbal communication related to panic anxiety, disordered, unrealistic thinking evidenced by loosening of associations, echolalia, verbalizations that reflect concrete thinking and poor eye contact.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: patient will be able to communicate appropriately and comprehensibly by the time of discharge.</p>
<p>Ineffective family coping related to highly ambivalent family relationships, impaired family communication evidenced by neglectful care of the patient, extreme denial or prolonged over-concern regarding his illness.</p>
<p>Goal/outcome: family will identify more adaptive coping strategies for dealing with patient's illness and treatment regimen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="course-and-prognosis">Course and prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#course-and-prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Complete remission is possible after an acute attack and the remission of symptoms, maintenance therapy should be continued for at least one year.</p>
<p>Negative symptoms: the presence of these indicates a poorer prognosis.</p>
<p>Sex: Females tend to be better socially adjusted.</p>
<p>Marital status: prognosis is better in those who are married.</p>
<p>Acute or gradual onset: prognosis is better in acute onset with a clear triggering factor as opposed to gradual onset.</p>
<p>Premorbid personality: premorbid social withdrawal and other schizoid traits predict a poor outcome. Those with social contacts outside the home have a better prognosis.</p>
<p>Comorbid disorders: these include depression, substance use and the presence of structural brain changes. The last two are associated with a poor prognosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="for-an-individual-to-be-diagnosed-as-having-schizophrenia-symptoms-must-persist-for-six-months-with-one-month-of-acute-symptoms">For an individual to be diagnosed as having schizophrenia, symptoms must persist for six months with one month of acute symptoms.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#for-an-individual-to-be-diagnosed-as-having-schizophrenia-symptoms-must-persist-for-six-months-with-one-month-of-acute-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="affective-disorders-mood-disorders">Affective Disorders (mood disorders)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#affective-disorders-mood-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are characterized by disturbance of mood, accompanied by full or partial manic or depressive syndrome, which is not due to any other physical or mental disorder.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-mood-disorders">Classification of mood disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-mood-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mood-affective-disorders">Mood (affective disorders)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood-affective-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Manic episode</li>
<li>Bipolar affective disorder</li>
<li>Depressive episode</li>
<li>Recurrent depressive disorder</li>
<li>Persistent mood disorder</li>
<li>Other mood disorders</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Unspecified mood disorder.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="manic-episode">Manic episode<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#manic-episode" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mania refers to a syndrome in which the central features are over-activity, mood change which maybe towards elation or irritability and self-important ideas.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-mania">Classification of mania<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-mania" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Manic episode</li>
<li>Hypomania</li>
<li>Mania without psychotic symptoms.</li>
<li>Mania with psychotic symptoms</li>
<li>Other manic episodes</li>
<li>Manic episode unspecified.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Related to excessive levels of norepinephrine and dopamine and a deficiency in serotonin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An acute mania is characterized by the following features which should last for at least one week</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="elevated-expansive-or-irritable-mood">Elevated, expansive or irritable mood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#elevated-expansive-or-irritable-mood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This has four stages depending on the severity of manic episodes:</p>
<p>Euphoria (stage 1): increased sense of psychological well-being and happiness not in keeping with ongoing events.</p>
<p>Elation (stage II): moderate elevation of mood with increased psychomotor activity.</p>
<p>Exaltation (stage III): Intense elevation of mood with delusions of grandeur.</p>
<p>Ecstasy (stage IV): Severe elevation of mood, intense sense of rupture or blissfulness seen in delirious or stuporous mania.</p>
<p>Expansive mood is increasing and unselective enthusiasm for interacting with people and surrounding environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychomotor-activity">Psychomotor activity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychomotor-activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There is increased activity ranging from over activeness and restlessness to manic excitement. The person involves in ceaseless activity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="speech-and-thought">Speech and thought<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#speech-and-thought" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Flight of ideas: thoughts racing in mind, rapid shifts from one topic to another.</p>
<p>Pressure of speech: speech is forceful, strong and difficult to interrupt. Uses playful language with punning, rhyming, joking and teasing and speaks loudly.</p>
<p>Delusions of grandeur.</p>
<p>Delusions of persecution.</p>
<p>Distractibility.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-features">Other features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Increased sociability.</li>
<li>Impulsive behaviour.</li>
<li>Disinhibition.</li>
<li>Hypersexual and promiscuous behaviour.</li>
<li>Poor judgment.</li>
<li>High risk activities (buying sprees, reckless driving, foolish business investments, distributing money or articles to unknown persons)</li>
<li>Dressed up in gaudy and flamboyant clothes although in severe mania there may be poor self-care.</li>
<li>Decreased need for sleep (&lt; 3 hours)</li>
<li>Decreased food intake due to over activity.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Decreased attention and concentration.</li>
<li>Poor judgment.</li>
<li>Absent insight.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-of-hypomania">Symptoms of hypomania<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-hypomania" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a lesser degree of mania.</li>
<li>There is persistent mild elevation of mood and increased sense of psychological well-being and happiness not in keeping with ongoing events.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Pharmacotherapy</strong>
Lithium: 900-2100 mg/day.
Carbamazepine 600-1800 mg/day
Sodium valproate 600-2600 mg/day
Other drugs: clonazepam, calcium channel blockers.</p>
<p><strong>Electroconvulsive therapy</strong>
For acute manic excitement if not adequately responding to antipsychotics and lithium.</p>
<p><strong>Psychosocial treatment</strong>
Family and marital therapy is used to decrease interfamilial and interpersonal difficulties and to reduce or modify stressors. The main purpose is to ensure continuity of treatment and adequate drug compliance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-management-for-mania">Nursing management for mania<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management-for-mania" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Nursing assessment</strong>
Assess the severity of the disorder, forming an opinion about the causes, assessing the patient's resources and judging the patient's behaviour on other people.
Relevant data should be collected from the patient as well as from his relatives, because the patient may not always recognize the extent of his abnormal behaviour.
During assessment the nurse should include mood and affect, thinking and perceptual ability, sleep disturbances, changes in energy level and character of speech patterns.
Mood and affect should be assessed for congruency.
Note the patterns of verbal speech.
The tone of voice, pace at which thoughts are processed and communicated and the rate at which are spoken are all relevant.
Assess for sleeping and eating patterns, energy levels and weight changes.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Objective signs of mania</th><th>Subjective signs of mania</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Disturbance of speech</td><td>Feelings of joy</td></tr><tr><td>Rapid speech</td><td>Rapid mood swings</td></tr><tr><td>Loud, pressured speech</td><td>Sleep disturbances</td></tr><tr><td>Easily distracted</td><td>Delusions</td></tr><tr><td>Over activity</td><td>hallucinations</td></tr><tr><td>Mood lability</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Weight changes</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><strong>Nursing diagnosis</strong>
High risk for injury related to extreme hyperactivity and impulsive behaviour, evidenced by lack of control over purposeless and potentially injurious movements.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>G/O: patient will not injure self.</p>
<p>High risk for violence; self-directed or directed at others related to manic excitement, delusional thinking and hallucinations.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will not harm self or others.</p>
<p>Altered nutrition, less than body requirements related to refusal to feed or inability to sit still long enough to eat, evidenced by weight loss, amenorrhoea.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will not exhibit signs and symptoms of malnutrition.</p>
<p>Impaired social interaction related to egocentric and narcissistic behaviour, evidenced by inability to develop satisfying relationships and manipulation for others for own desires.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will interact with others in an appropriate manner.</p>
<p>Self-esteem disturbance related to unmet dependency needs, lack of positive feedback, unrealistic self-expectations.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will have realistic expectations about self.</p>
<p>Altered family processes related to euphoric mood and grandiose ideas, manipulative behaviour, refusal to accept responsibility for own actions.</p>
<p>G/O: the family members will demonstrate coping ability in dealing with the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="depressive-episode">DEPRESSIVE EPISODE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#depressive-episode" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Definition: characterized by one or more depressive episodes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Depressive episode</p>
<p>Mild depressive episode</p>
<p>Moderate depressive episode</p>
<p>Severe D.E without psychotic symptoms</p>
<p>Other depressive episodes- atypical depression.</p>
<p>Depressive episode, unspecified.</p>
<p>Recurrent depressive disorder.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is due to negative cognitions which include:</p>
<p>Negative expectation of the environment, self and the future. These cognitive distortions arise out of defect in cognitive development and cause an individual to feel inadequate, worthless and rejected by others.</p>
<p>Stressful life events for example death, marriage, financial loss before the onset of a disease.</p>
<p>This result in the levels of norepinephrine and serotonin are decreased and deregulation of acetylcholine and GABA.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Characterized by the following features, which should last for at least two weeks in order to make a diagnosis?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="depressed-mood">Depressed mood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#depressed-mood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sadness of mood or loss of interest and loss of pleasure in almost all activities (pervasive sadness), present throughout the day (persistent sadness)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="depressive-cognitions">Depressive cognitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#depressive-cognitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hopelessness (a feeling of no hope in future due to pessimism)</p>
<p>Helplessness (the patient feels that no help is possible)</p>
<p>Worthlessness (a feeling of inadequacy and inferiority)</p>
<p>Unreasonable guilt and self-blame over trivial matters in the past.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="suicidal-thoughts">Suicidal thoughts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#suicidal-thoughts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ideas of hopelessness are often accompanied by the thought that life is no longer worth living and that death has come as a welcome release. These gloomy preoccupations may progress to thoughts of plans for suicide.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychomotor-activity">Psychomotor activity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychomotor-activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Psychomotor retardation is frequent. The retarded patient thinks and acts slowly. Slowing of thoughts is reflected in the patient's speech; questions are often answers after a long delay and in monotonous voice.</p>
<p>In older patients, agitation is common with marked anxiety, restlessness and feelings of uneasiness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="somatic-melancholic-features-symptoms-of-depression">Somatic (melancholic features) symptoms of depression<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#somatic-melancholic-features-symptoms-of-depression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Significant decrease in appetite or weight.</li>
<li>Early morning awakening at 2 or more hours before the usual time of waking up.</li>
<li>Diurnal variation, with depression being worse in the morning.</li>
<li>Pervasive lack of interest and lack of reactivity to pleasurable stimuli.</li>
<li>Psychomotor agitation or retardation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-symptoms">Other symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Difficulty in thinking and concentration.</li>
<li>Subjective poor memory.</li>
<li>Menstrual or sexual disturbances.</li>
<li>Vague physical symptoms such as fatigue, discomfort, constipation, thoughts of death, decreased libido, dependency, spontaneous crying, and passiveness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Psychopharmacology: antidepressants</li>
<li>ECT: for severe depression with suicidal risk.</li>
<li>Psychological treatment</li>
<li>Psychotherapy based on psychoanalytic interventions emphasizes helping patients gain insight into the cause of the depression.</li>
<li>Cognitive therapy: aims at correcting the depressive negative cognitions like hopelessness, worthlessness, helplessness and pessimistic ideas and replacing them with new cognitive and behavioural responses.</li>
<li>Supportive psychotherapy</li>
<li>Group therapy: negative feelings such as anxiety, anger, guilt, despair are recognized and emotional growth is improved through expression of their feelings.</li>
<li>Family therapy</li>
<li>Behavioral therapy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-management-of-major-depression-episode">Nursing management of major depression episode<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management-of-major-depression-episode" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="nursing-assessment">Nursing assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Should focus on judging the severity of the disorder including the risk of suicide, identifying the possible causes, the social resources available to the patient, and the effect of the disorder on other people.</p>
<p>Although there is a risk of suicide in every depressed patient, the risk is much more in the presence of the following factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Presence of marked helplessness.</li>
<li>Male sex</li>
<li>More than 40 years of age</li>
<li>Unmarried, widowed or divorced.</li>
<li>Written or verbal communication of suicidal intent or plan.</li>
<li>Early stages of depression.</li>
<li>Recovery from depression (at the peak of depression the patient is usually either too depressed or too retarded to commit suicide)</li>
<li>Period of three months from recovery. The nurse should routinely enquire about the patient's work, finances, family life, social activities, general living conditions and physical health.</li>
</ul>
<p>50 | Page</p>
<p>It is also important to consider whether a patient could endanger other people, particularly if there are depressive delusions and the patient may act on them.</p>
<p>Observe for mood, affect, thinking, perceptual ability, somatic complaints, sleep disturbances and changes in energy levels.</p>
<p>Determine the amount of assistance required for personal hygiene and elimination needs.</p>
<p>Assess for any suicidal ideation and whether a plan has been devised.</p>
<p>Assess for objective signs and subjective symptoms.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Objective signs</th><th>Subjective symptoms</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Alterations of activity</td><td>Anhedonia</td></tr><tr><td>Poor personal hygiene</td><td>Worthlessness, hopelessness, helplessness.</td></tr><tr><td>Apathy</td><td>Suicidal ideas.</td></tr><tr><td>Altered social interactions</td><td>Impairment of cognition</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Delusions</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>hallucinations</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Nursing diagnosis</p>
<p>High risk of self-directed violence related to depressed mood, feelings of worthlessness and anger directed inward towards self.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will not harm self.</p>
<p>Dysfunctional grieving related to real or perceived loss, bereavement evidenced by denial of loss, inappropriate expression of anger, inability to carry out activities of daily living.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will be able to verbalize normal behaviours associated with grieving.</p>
<p>Powerlessness related to dysfunctional grieving process, life style of helplessness evidenced by feelings of lack of control over life situations, over-dependence on others to fulfill needs.</p>
<p>G/O: the patient will be able to take control of life situations.</p>
<p>Self-esteem disturbance related to learned helplessness, impaired cognition, negative view of self, evidenced by expression of worthlessness, sensitivity to criticism, negative and pessimistic outlook.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will be able to verbalize positive aspects about self and attempt new activities without fear of failure.</p>
<p>Altered communication process related to depressive cognitions, evidenced by being unable to interact with others, withdrawn, expressing fear of failure or rejection.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will communicate or interact with staff or other patients in the unit.</p>
<p>Altered sleep and rest related to depressed mood and depressive cognitions evidenced by difficulty in falling asleep, early morning awakening, verbal complaints of not feeling well rested.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will sleep adequately during the night.</p>
<p>Altered nutrition, less than body requirements related to depressed mood, lack of appetite or lack of interest in food, evidenced by weight loss, poor muscle tone, pale conjunctiva, poor skin turgor.</p>
<p>G/O: patient's nutritional status will improve.</p>
<p>Self-care deficit related to depressed mood, feelings of worthlessness, evidenced by poor personal hygiene and grooming.</p>
<p>G/O: patient will maintain adequate personal hygiene.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bipolar-mood-disorder-bipolar-affective-disorder-manic-depressive-disorder">BIPOLAR MOOD DISORDER(BIPOLAR AFFECTIVE DISORDER,MANIC DEPRESSIVE DISORDER)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bipolar-mood-disorder-bipolar-affective-disorder-manic-depressive-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is characterized by recurrent episodes of mania and depression in the same patient at different times. Typically the patient experiences extreme highs (mania and hypomania) alternating with extreme lows (depression); interspersed between the highs and lows are periods of normal mood.</p>
<p>Onset usually occurs between ages 20 and 30 years.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Exact cause is unknown but is thought that genetic, biochemical and psychological factors may play a role.</p>
<p>Maybe triggered by stressful events, antidepressant use.</p>
<p>Sleep deprivation and hypothyroidism.</p>
<p>Signs and symptoms</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Manic phase</th><th>Depressive phase</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Expansive, grandiose, or hyperirritable mood.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Increased psychomotor activity such as agitation, pacing or hand wringing.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Excessive social extroversion</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Rapid speech with frequent topic changes</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Decreased need for sleep and food</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Impulsivity</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Impaired judgement</td><td>Low self esteem</td></tr><tr><td>Overwhelming inertia</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Feelings of hopelessness, apathy or self-reproach.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Difficulty concentrating or thinking clearly (without obvious disorientation or intellectual impairment)</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Psychomotor retardation</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Anhedonia</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Suicidal ideation</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Lithium</li>
<li>Valporoic acid</li>
<li>Carbamazepine</li>
<li>Antidepressants</li>
<li>Antipsychotics.</li>
</ul>
<p>Course and prognosis of mood disorders</p>
<p>An average manic episode lasts for 3-4 months, while a depressive disorder lasts for 4-9 months.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organic-brain-disorders">ORGANIC BRAIN DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organic-brain-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are mental disorders as a result of medical conditions which induce brain dysfunction and lead to the appearance of characteristic psychological symptoms.</p>
<p>Causes of brain dysfunction</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Infections (cerebral)</th><th>Malaria (falciparum); typhoid fever; syphilis; trypanasomiasis; bacterial meningitis; viral meningitis; toxoplasmosis; HIV/AIDS.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Infections (systemic)</td><td>Septicemia; typhoid fever; bronchopneumonia;</td></tr><tr><td>Hypoxia</td><td>Carbon monoxide poisoning</td></tr><tr><td>Metabolic</td><td>Electrolyte imbalance; vitamin B deficiency; porphyria; liver and renal diseases; spontaneous hypoglycemia</td></tr><tr><td>Endocrine</td><td>Thyrotoxicosis; myxodema' cushing's syndrome; diabetic ketoacidosis.</td></tr><tr><td>Cerebral tumor</td><td>Primary; metastaic</td></tr><tr><td>Head injury</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Vascular disease</td><td>Sub-arachnoid hemorrhage; multi-infact dementia</td></tr><tr><td>Degenerative disease</td><td>Alzheimer's disease</td></tr><tr><td>Substance use</td><td>Alcohol; barbiturates; cannabis; hallucinogens.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dementia-in-alzheimer-s-disease-chronic-organic-brain-syndrome">DEMENTIA IN ALZHEIMER'S DISEASE (CHRONIC ORGANIC BRAIN SYNDROME)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dementia-in-alzheimer-s-disease-chronic-organic-brain-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Refers to the chronic progressive brain dysfunction that leads to impaired memory, personality changes and intellectual deterioration but without impairment of consciousness.</p>
<p>Alzheimer's disease: this is a chronic neurodegenerative disease that usually starts slowly and gets worse overtime.</p>
<p>There are two types: presenile dementia that occurs before the age of 65 years and senile dementia that occurs after the age of 65 years</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-dementia">Stages of dementia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-dementia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Stage I: early stage (2-4 years)</p>
<p>Forgetfulness.</p>
<p>Declining interest in environment.</p>
<p>Hesitancy in initiating actions.</p>
<p>Poor performance at work.</p>
<p>Stage II: middle stage (2 to 12 years)</p>
<p>Progressive memory loss</p>
<p>Hesitates in response to questions</p>
<p>Has difficulty in following simple instructions.</p>
<p>Irritable, anxious.</p>
<p>Neglects personal hygiene.</p>
<p>Social isolation.</p>
<p>Stage III: final stage (upto a year)</p>
<p>Marked loss of weight because of inadequate food intake.</p>
<p>Unable to communicate.</p>
<p>Does not recognize family.</p>
<p>Incontinence of urine and feces.</p>
<p>Loses the ability to stand and walk.</p>
<p>Death is usually caused by aspiration pneumonia.</p>
