<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7195d1bd">Clinical features (for Alzheimer’s type)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7195d1bd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Personality changes: Lack of interest in day to day activities, easy mental fatigability, self-centered, withdrawn, decreased self-care.</p>
<p>Memory impairment: recent memory is prominently affected.</p>
<p>Cognitive impairment: disorientation, poor judgment, difficulty in abstraction, decreased attention span.</p>
<p>Affective impairment: labile mood, irritableness, depression.</p>
<p>Behavioural impairment: stereotyped behaviour alteration in sexual drives and activities, neurotic/psychotic behaviour.</p>
<p>Neurological impairment: aphasia, apraxia, agnosia, seizures, headache.</p>
<p>Catastrophic reaction: agitation, attempt to compensate for defects by using strategies to avoid demonstrating failures in intellectual performances, such as changing the subject, cracking jokes or otherwise diverting the interviewer.</p>
<p>Sundowner syndrome: it is characterized by drowsiness, confusion, ataxia, accidental falls may occur at night when external stimuli such as light and interpersonal orienting cues are diminished.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The main aim of treatment is to maintain the patient in the community.</p>
<p>Pharmacological methods:</p>
<p>Antipsychotic medications such as risperidone and haloperidol maybe used to decrease verbal and physical aggressiveness to alleviate hallucinations and delusions.</p>
<p>Benzodiazepines for insomnia and anxiety.</p>
<p>Antidepressants for depression.</p>
<p>Anticonvulsants to control seizures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="nursing-assessment">Nursing assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Assessment data includes the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disorientation</li>
<li>Mood changes</li>
<li>Fear</li>
<li>Suspiciousness</li>
<li>Self-care deficit</li>
<li>Social behavior</li>
<li>Level of mobility, wandering behavior.</li>
<li>Judgement ability</li>
<li>Sleep disturbance</li>
<li>Speech or language impairment</li>
<li>Hallucinations, illusions or delusions</li>
<li>Bowel and bladder incontinence</li>
<li>Apathy</li>
<li>Any decline in nutritional status</li>
<li>Recognition of family members</li>
<li>Identify primary care giver, support system and the knowledge base of family members.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-interventions">Nursing interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="daily-routine">Daily routine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily-routine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Maintaining a daily routine includes drawing a fixed timetable for the patient for waking up in the morning, toilet, exercise and meals. This gives the patient a sense of security. Patient often deteriorate after dark, a phenomenon known as sundowning. Additional care must be taken during the evening and at night. Orient the patient to reality in order to</p>
<p>54 | Page</p>
<p>decrease confusion. Provide newspapers which stimulate interest in current events. Orientation of place, person and time should be given before approaching the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nutrition-and-body-weight">Nutrition and body weight<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition-and-body-weight" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Provide a balanced diet. Allow plenty of time for meals. Tell the patient which meal it is and what is there to be eaten, food served should neither be too cold nor too hot.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-hygiene">Personal hygiene<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This includes brushing of teeth, bathing, keeping the skin clean and dry, particularly in areas prone to perspiration, such as the armpits and the groin.</p>
<p>Nail care for those unable to. They may have a problem with the lock on the bathroom door, if this happens it is advisable to remove the lock.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="toilet-habits-and-incontinence">Toilet habits and incontinence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toilet-habits-and-incontinence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Toilet habits should be established as soon as possible and maintained as a rigid routine. This includes conditioned behavior such as going for bowel movement immediately after a cup of tea. The patient should be taken to urinate at fixed interval.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="accidents">Accidents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#accidents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Great care should be taken to avoid accidents caused by tripping over furniture; falling down the stairs or slipping in the bathroom. Let the patients wear fitting shoes. They should be gently persuaded to stop driving as this can pose a hazard to them and others. Do not allow the patient to take medication alone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mood-and-emotions">Mood and emotions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood-and-emotions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some patients have abrupt change in their moods and emotions. These changes can be unpredictable. Mood changes are best controlled by keeping a calm environment with fixed daily routine. The patient should not be questioned repeatedly or given too many choices, such what they want to eat or what they want to wear. Mood changes are also responsive to distraction, particularly if topics related to the past are discussed or favorite music played which puts them in a nostalgic mood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wandering">Wandering<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wandering" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These patients often lose their geographic orientation and can even get lost in familiar surroundings. They may be found wandering aimlessly either in the neighborhood or far away. It is advisable to have some identification bracelet or card always in their possession. The doors of the house should be securely locked so that the patients cannot leave unnoticed. The patient should always be accompanied while going for walks or for simple chores outside the house.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disturbed-sleep">Disturbed sleep<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disturbed-sleep" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sleep disturbances are extremely distressing to the family. If the patient is restless at night or wanders and talks at night, the entire family is disturbed. Sleep patterns must be maintained. Napping during the day should be avoided.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="interpersonal-relationship">Interpersonal relationship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interpersonal-relationship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Verbal communication should be clear and unhurried. Questions that require yes or no answers are best. Give necessary information repeatedly. Try to make sure that each day has something of interest for the patient-it might be going for a walk, listening to music, talk about the day's activities. Try to involve old friends for a chat about the past.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delirium">DELIRIUM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delirium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is an acute organic mental disorder characterized by impairment of consciousness, disorientation and disturbances in perception and restlessness. There are additional features such as restlessness, illusions and psychotic features in the form of auditory or visual hallucinations and delusions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main symptom and sign is the clouding of consciousness (GCS less or equal to 8)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Eye opening</th><th>Best verbal response</th><th>Best motor response</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>5. Normal</td><td>5. Oriented</td><td>5. Obeys verbal commands</td></tr><tr><td>4. Spontaneous</td><td>4. Confused but talking in sentences.</td><td>4. Localizing to pain.</td></tr><tr><td>3. To speech</td><td>3. Uttering inappropriate sounds</td><td>3. Flexion to pain</td></tr><tr><td>2. To pain</td><td>2. Incomprehensible sounds (no</td><td>2. Extension to pain.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>55 | Page</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>words)</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1. None</td><td>1. None</td><td>1. None</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Impairment of attention: difficulty in shifting, focusing and sustaining attention.</p>
<p>Perceptual disturbances: illusions and hallucinations most often visual.</p>
<p>Disturbance of cognition: impairment of abstract thinking and comprehension, impairment of immediate and recent memory, increased reaction time.</p>
<p>Psychomotor disturbance: hypo or hyperactivity. aimless groping or picking at the bed cloths (flocculation), enhanced startle reaction.</p>
<p>Disturbance in the sleep-wake cycle: insomnia or in severe cases total sleep loss or reversal in the sleep wake cycle, daytime drowsiness, nocturnal worsening of symptoms, disturbing dreams or nightmares, which may continue as hallucinations after awakening.</p>
<p>Emotional disturbances: depression, anxiety, fear, irritability, euphoria, apathy.</p>
<p>Course and prognosis</p>
<p>The onset is usually abrupt. The duration of an episode is usually brief, lasting for about a week.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pharmacotherapy: identification of cause and its immediate correction, for example, 50mg of 50% dextrose IV for hypoglycemia, oxygen for hypoxia, 100mg of vitamin B one IV for thiamine deficiency, IV fluids for fluid and electrolyte imbalance.</p>
<p>Benzodiazepines for</p>
<p>Antipsychotics for</p>
<p>Nursing intervention</p>
<p>Providing safe environment</p>
<p>Restrict environmental stimuli, keep unit calm and well illuminated.</p>
<p>There should be always somebody at the patient bedside reassuring and supporting.</p>
<p>As the patient is responding to a terrifying unrealistic world of hallucinatory hallucinations and delusions, special precautions are needed to protect him from himself and to protect others.</p>
<p>Alleviating patient's fear and anxiety:</p>
<p>Remove any object in the room that seems to be a source of misinterpreted perception.</p>
<p>As much as possible have the same person all the time by the patient's bedside.</p>
<p>Keep the room well lighted especially at night.</p>
<p>Meeting the physical needs of the patients</p>
<p>Appropriate care should be provided after physical assessment.</p>
<p>Use appropriate nursing measures to reduce fever if present.</p>
<p>Maintain intake and output chart.</p>
<p>Mouth and skin should be taken care of.</p>
<p>Monitor vital signs.</p>
<p>Observe patient for any extreme drowsiness and sleep as this maybe an indication that the patient is slipping into a coma.</p>
<p>Facilitate orientation</p>
<p>Repeatedly explain to the patient where he is and what date, day and time it is.</p>
<p>Introduce people with name even if the patient misidentifies the people.</p>
<p>Have a calendar in the room and tell him what day it is.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organic-amnestic-syndrome">ORGANIC AMNESTIC SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organic-amnestic-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There is impairment or loss of recent memory with preservation of immediate recall, remote memory and other cognitive functions due to an underlying organic course.</p>
<p>There is no disturbance of consciousness.</p>
<p>The most common cause for this condition is thiamine deficiency as a result of chronic alcoholism. It is also called as "Wernicke's-Korsakoff syndrome."</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Wernicke’s encephalopathy is an acute phase of delirium preceding amnestic syndrome, while Korsakoff syndrome is a chronic phase of amnestic syndrome.</p>
<p>Clinical features</p>
<p>Recent memory impairment.</p>
<p>Anterograde and retrograde amnesia.</p>
<p>There is no impairment of recent memory.</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>Treatment for underlying cause.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neuroses">NEUROSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neuroses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a less severe form of psychiatry disorder where patients show either excessive or prolonged emotional reaction to any given stress.</p>
<p>These disorders are not caused by organic disease of the brain and however severe, do not involve hallucinations and delusions.</p>
<p>Maybe classified as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Generalized anxiety disorder (GAD)</li>
<li>Panic disorder.</li>
<li>Phobic disorders.</li>
<li>Obsessive compulsive disorder (OCD)</li>
<li>Post-traumatic stress disorder (PTSD)</li>
</ul>
<p>Secondary to general medical condition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anxiety is a state of tension and apprehension with hyperactivity of the autonomic nervous system as a natural response to perceived threat.</p>
<p>The frequency and intensity of anxiety responses are out of proportion when compared to situations that trigger them.</p>
<p>Anxiety may interfere with daily life.</p>
<p>These disorders have three components:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cognitive components: subjective feeling of apprehension, a sense of impending danger and a feeling of inability to cope.</li>
<li>Physiological response: increased heart rate, Bp, muscle tension, rapid breathing, dry mouth, diarrhea and frequent urination.</li>
<li>Behavioural responses: avoidance of certain situations and impaired task performance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="generalized-anxiety-disorder-gad">GENERALIZED ANXIETY DISORDER (GAD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generalized-anxiety-disorder-gad" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a disorder in which there is persistent and excessive feelings of anxiety not attached to any particular</p>
<p>pecific situations, but rather caused by a general tendency to worry excessively.</p>
<p>Anxiety may last for months with the signs almost present continuously. There is a sense of impending disaster, though not specific.</p>
<p>Typical worries include excessive worries about work or social performance, exaggerated concerns about finances and the possibility of becoming ill or having an accident.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-symptoms-of-gad">Common symptoms of GAD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-symptoms-of-gad" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Psychological: fearful anticipation, irritability, sensitivity to noise, restlessness, poor concentration, worrying thoughts and apprehension.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical">Physical<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Gastrointestinal: dry mouth, difficulty in swallowing, epigastric discomfort, frequent or loose motions.</p>
<p>Respiratory: constriction in the chest, difficulty inhaling, over-breathing.</p>
<p>Genitourinary: frequency or urgent micturition, failure of erection, menstrual discomfort, amenorrhea.</p>
<p>Neuromuscular system: tremor, prickling sensations, tinnitus, dizziness, headache, aching muscles.</p>
<p>Sleep disturbances: insomnia, night terrors.</p>
<p>Other symptoms: depression, obsessions, depersonalization, derealization.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>pharmacotherapy</li>
<li>Antianxiety drugs</li>
<li>Antidepressants</li>
<li>SSRIs</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>57 | Page</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Beta blockers.</p>
<p>Behavioural therapy: teach the patient how to become aware of them and then consciously control various body functions (vital signs). Relaxation techniques e.g. Yoga, meditation.</p>
<p>Cognitive therapy: by teaching the patient how to restructure her thoughts and view her worries more realistically. A patient may be taught to record worries and lists evidence that justifies or contradicts each one. Patient learns that worrying about worry maintain anxiety; avoidance and procrastination are ineffective problem solving techniques.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="panic-disorder">PANIC DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#panic-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is characterized by anxiety, which is intermittent and unrelated to particular circumstances. It is a discrete period of intense fear or discomfort, in which four or more of the following symptoms developed abruptly and reached a peak within 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Palpitations, pounding heart or accelerated heart rate.</p>
<p>Sweating.</p>
<p>Trembling or shaking.</p>
<p>Sensations of shortness of breath or smothering.</p>
<p>Feeling of choking.</p>
<p>Chest pain or discomfort.</p>
<p>Nausea or abdominal distress.</p>
<p>Feeling dizzy, unsteady, lightheaded or faint.</p>
<p>Derealization (feeling of unreality) or depersonalization (being detached from oneself)</p>
<p>Fear of losing control or going crazy.</p>
<p>Fear of dying.</p>
<p>Paresthesias (numbness or tingling sensation)</p>
<p>Chills or hot flushes.</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>Pharmacotherapy: benzodiazepines; antidepressants, beta blockers to control severe palpitations that have not responded to anxiolytics.</p>
<p>Behavioural therapy</p>
<p>Relaxation techniques to help patient cope with panic attack by easing physical symptoms and directing attention elsewhere.</p>
<p>Deep breath relaxation, which involves tightening and relaxation of the skeletal muscles in a sequential fashion.</p>
<p>Positive verbalization or guided imagery, in which the patient elicits peaceful mental images or some other purposeful thought or action, promoting feelings of relaxation, renewed hope, and a sense of being in control of a stressful situation.</p>
<p>Listening to calming music.</p>
<p>Cognitive therapy</p>
<p>Teaches the patient to replace negative thoughts with more realistic, positive ways of viewing the attacks.</p>
<p>Helps the patient to identify possible triggers for the panic attacks, such as a particular situation or thought or even a slight change in heartbeat.</p>
<p>Helps the patient to identify and evaluate the thoughts that precede anxiety and then restructures them to gain a more realistic perception.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="phobic-anxiety-disorder">PHOBIC ANXIETY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phobic-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A phobia is an unreasonable fear of a specific object, activity or situation. This fear is disproportionate to the circumstances that precipitate it. It cannot be dealt with by reasoning or controlled by will power. The individual avoids the feared object or situation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-phobia">TYPES OF PHOBIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-phobia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Simple, social, agoraphobia and specific phobias.</p>
<p>Simple (specific) phobia</p>
<p>It is an irrational fear of a specific object or stimulus. Common in childhood.</p>
<p>Examples of some specific phobias</p>
<p>Acrophobia: fear of heights.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Hematophobia: fear of the sight blood.
Claustrophobia: fear of closed spaces.
Gamaphobia: fear of marriage.
Insectophobia: fear of insects.
AIDS phobia:
Zoophobia: animals
Microphobia: germs
Brontophobia: thunder
Algophobia: pain
Social phobia
It is an irrational fear of performing activities in the presence of other people or interacting with others. The patient is afraid of his own actions being viewed by others. Critically, resulting in embarrassment or humiliation.
S&amp;S of S.phobia
Hyperventilation
Sweating, cold clammy hands.
Blushing.
Palpitations
GIT symptoms
Trembling hands and voice
Urinary urgency
Muscle tension
Anticipatory anxiety
Fear of embarrassment or ridicule.
Many people who have social phobia are under achievers because of test anxiety, poor job performance, or poor communication skills. They may have few or no friends, a decreased support system and poor interpersonal relationships.
Agoraphobia
This is characterized by an irrational fear of being in places away from familiar setting of home, in crowds or in situations that the patient cannot leave easily.
As the agoraphobia increases in severity, there is gradual restriction in normal day to day activities
S&amp;S
Overriding fear of open or public spaces.
Deep concern that help might not be available in such places.
Avoidance of public places and confinement to home.
Course and prognosis
More common in women. Onset is sudden without any cause. The course is usually chronic. Sometimes phobias are spontaneous remitting.
Management
Pharmacotherapy: BZ and antidepressants.
Behavioral therapy
Desensitization therapy to gradually reintroduce the feared situation while coaching the patient on relaxation techniques.
Role playing in guided imagery to allow the patient to rehearse ways to relax while confronting a feared object or situation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obsessive-compulsive-disorder">Obsessive compulsive disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Either obsessions (thoughts of being infected by germs) or compulsions (behavioral-washing and cleaning rituals)
Obsessions defined as:
Repetitive and persistent thoughts, impulses, or images that are experienced at some time during the disturbance, as intrusive and inappropriate that intrude an individual's consciousness and that causes marked anxiety or distress. They are often abhorrent (distasteful) to the person, but very difficult to dismiss or control.
The thoughts, impulses or images are not simply excessive worries about real life problems.
The person attempts to ignore or suppress such thoughts, impulses or images or to neutralize them with some other thought or action.
The person recognizes that the obsessional thoughts, impulses or images are a product of his or her own mind.</p>
<p>This document is available on
59 | Page
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Compulsions (focus on contamination) defined as:</p>
<p>Repetitive, persistent and uncontrollable behavioural urges to perform certain behaviours (e.g. hand-washing, ordering, checking things repeatedly, cleaning, counting) or mental acts (e.g. praying, counting, repeating words silently) resisted only with great difficulty. That the person feels driven to perform in response to an obsession or according to rules that must be applied rigidly and in a specific order. Failure to perform the compulsive acts leads to tremendous intensity of anxiety.</p>
<p>The behaviours or mental acts are aimed at preventing or reducing distress or preventing some dreaded event or situation; however these behaviours or mental acts either are not connected in a realistic way with what they are designed to neutralize or prevent or are clearly excessive.</p>
<p>OCD may lead to avoidance of certain objects or situations (e.g. dirt and not leaving the house to avoid unlocking doors); life disruption; frustration; irritation to an individual, family, friends, workmates, depression and anxiety.</p>
<p>Management</p>
<p>Pharmacotherapy: antidepressants, anxiolytics.</p>
<p>Behavioral therapy:</p>
<p>Exposure and response prevention e.g. compulsive hand washers are encouraged to touch contaminated objects and then refrain from washing in order to break the negative reinforcement chain.</p>
<p>Thought stoppage:</p>
<p>This is a technique to help an individual to learn to stop thinking unwanted thoughts. Ask the patient to bring to mind the unwanted thought concentrating only on one thought per procedure.</p>
<p>As soon as the thought forms, give the command “Stop.” follow this with calm and deliberate diversion of thought to something pleasant.</p>
<p>Repeat the procedure to bring the unwanted thought under control.</p>
<p>Relaxation technique: it includes deep breathing exercises, progressive muscle relaxation, meditation, imagery and music.</p>
<p>POST TRAUMATIC DISORDER</p>
<p>This is a long-lasting anxiety response following a traumatic or catastrophic event.</p>
<p>Typically traumatic events include violent assault; being kidnapped; held a prisoner at war; victim of manmade or natural disasters, being diagnosed with life-threatening illness, torture, terrorist attack and witnessing or learning about unexpected death of another person.</p>
<p>Usually PTSD develops within 3-6 months of the traumatic event. Major symptoms include:</p>
<p>Severe symptoms of anxiety, arousal and distress that was not present before the trauma on exposure to trauma cues.</p>
<p>Relieving the traumatic event recurrently in “flashbacks” dreams, images and fantasy.</p>
<p>Nightmares and disturbed sleep.</p>
<p>Becoming numb to the world and avoiding stimuli that remind one of the traumas.</p>
<p>Being easily startled.</p>
<p>Amnesia about important aspects of the traumatic event.</p>
<p>Concentration and memory difficulties.</p>
<p>Depressed or irritable mood.</p>
<p>Social withdrawal.</p>
<p>Experiencing extreme guilt about surviving the catastrophe when others did not.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The general approach is to provide emotional support; to encourage recall of the traumatic events. BZ may be needed to reduce anxiety.</p>
<p>Establish trusting relationship.</p>
<p>Encourage patient to express her grief, complete the mourning process.</p>
<p>Encourage move from physical to verbal expressions of anger.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personality-disorders">PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Personality is the relatively stable and predictable emotional and behavioural traits that characterize persons in their day to day living. They assist an individual to respond to wide range of situations.</p>
<p>When these traits are inflexible and maladaptive and causing distress and impairment in the functional abilities of an individual they constitute a personality disorder. These represent significant deviations from the way average individuals in a given culture perceive think, feel and relate to one another.</p>
<p>Individuals with PD are often unaware of their conditions and are likely to reject treatment.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>There symptoms are alloplastic (capable of adopting and altering external environment) and egosyntonic (acceptable to the ego). As a result they are not anxious and routinely ignore complaints from other members of the society.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>CLUSTER A (odd and eccentric): paranoid. Schizoid, schizotypal personality disorders.</p>
<p>CLUSTER B (dramatic, emotional and erratic): antisocial, histrionic, narcissistic personality disorders.</p>
<p>CLUSTER C (anxious and fearful): avoidant, dependent and OCD</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-personality-disorders">TYPES OF PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cluster-a-pd">CLUSTER A PD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cluster-a-pd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="paranoid-personality-disorder">Paranoid personality disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paranoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>This is characterized by persistent and long standing suspicion, sensitivity and mistrust of people.</p>
<p>They avoid responsibility for their actions, blame others, are hostile, angry and irritable and often interpret the actions of other people as being deliberately demeaning and threatening.</p>
<p>They tend to be pathologically jealous and argumentative.</p>
<p>They are usually un-emotional and fail to maintain friendly relationships.</p>
<p>In some cases they may show stubbornness and feeling of self-importance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="schizoid-personality-disorder">Schizoid personality disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>This is characterized by patient display a lifelong pattern of detachment and social withdrawal.</p>
<p>They are emotionally cold, self-sufficient, detached and have limited ability to express warmth or anger towards others.</p>
<p>They prefer solitary activities (e.g. reading) and are preoccupied with a variety of fantasies.</p>
<p>They generally lead a lonely life.</p>
<p>Their sexual life may exist only in fantasy and they often remain unmarried.</p>
<p>They prefer lonely non-competitive solitary jobs that other people find difficult to tolerate and tend to work at night to avoid contact with others.</p>
<p>They lack close friends or confidants other than first degree relatives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="schizotypal-personality-disorder">Schizotypal personality disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizotypal-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>The patients are eccentric, suspicious and show poor interpersonal relationships.</p>
<p>They are strikingly odd even to lay people and have a tendency to experience extrasensory perception e.g. telepathy including magical thinking and superstitions. On examination:</p>
<p>Inappropriate affect, odd thinking and speech (vague, circumstantial, metaphorical, overelaborate or stereotyped) odd beliefs or magical thinking that influences behaviour and is inconsistent with subcultural norms (e.g. superstitiousness, belief in clairvoyance, telepathy or 6th sense), social withdrawal, odd, eccentric or peculiar behaviour, lack of close relationships, social isolation, not fitting easily with others.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cluster-b-personality-disorder">CLUSTER B PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cluster-b-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Antisocial (dissocial) personality disorder (sociopath, psychopath)</p>
<p>This is characterized by chronic antisocial behavior that violates other rights or social norms which predisposes the affected person to criminal behaviour. The person is unable to maintain consistent, responsible functioning at work, school or as a parent. S&amp;S are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Failure to sustain relationships</li>
<li>Failure to conform to social norms with respect to lawful behaviours as indicated by repeatedly performing acts that are grounds for arrest.</li>
<li>Deceitfulness, as indicated by repeated lying, using of aliases, or conning others for personal profit or pleasure.</li>
<li>Disregard for the feelings of others</li>
<li>Impulsivity or failure to plan ahead.</li>
<li>Irritability and aggressiveness, as indicated by repeated physical fights or assaults.</li>
<li>Consistent irresponsibility, as indicated by repeated failure to sustain consistent work behavior or honor financial obligations.</li>
<li>Lack of remorse, as indicated by being indifferent to or rationalizing having hurt, mistreated or stolen from another.</li>
<li>Histrionic personality behaviour</li>
</ul>
