<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This type is characterized by excessive display of emotions, dramatization and extroversion. The individual has attention seeking behaviour and over concerned with physical attractiveness. There relationships are superficial and don't last long. They tend to be dependent on others, demanding and have endless need for reassurance.</p>
<p>They have a pervasive pattern of excessive emotionality and attention seeking, beginning by early adulthood and present in a variety of contexts as indicated by the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Is uncomfortable in situations in which he or she is not the center of attention.</li>
<li>Interaction with others is often characterized by inappropriate sexually seductive or provocative behaviour.</li>
<li>Displays rapidly shifting and shallow expression of emotions.</li>
<li>Consistently uses physical appearance to draw attention to self.</li>
<li>Has a style of speech that is excessively impressionistic and lacking in detail.</li>
<li>Shows self-dramatization, theatricality, and other exaggerated expression of emotions.</li>
<li>Is suggestible i.e. easily influenced by others or circumstances.</li>
<li>Considers relationships to be more intimate than they actually are.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="narcissistic-personality-disorder">Narcissistic personality disorder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcissistic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Narcissism is a pattern of grandiosity, need for admiration and lack of empathy. Narcissistic individuals have a heightened sense of self importance and entitlement. They believe they are unique in some way and behave accordingly. They are envious of others, arrogant and expect favors. Affected persons have fragile self-esteem and are prone to develop depression.</p>
<p>They have the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Has a grandiose sense of self-importance (e.g. exaggerates achievements and talents, expects to be recognized as superior without commensurate achievements)</li>
<li>Is preoccupied with fantasies of unlimited success, power, brilliance, beauty or ideal love.</li>
<li>Believes that he or she is "special" and unique and can only be understood by, or should associate with, other special or high status people (or institutions)</li>
<li>Requires excessive admiration.</li>
<li>Has a sense of entitlement i.e. unreasonable expectations of especially favorable treatment or automatic compliance with his or her expectations.</li>
<li>Is interpersonally exploitative i.e. takes advantage of others to achieve his or her own ends.</li>
<li>Lacks empathy: is unwilling to recognize or identify with the feelings and needs of others.</li>
<li>Is often envious of others or believes that others are envious of him or her.</li>
<li>Shows arrogant, haughty behaviours or attitudes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cluster-c-personality-disorder">CLUSTER C PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cluster-c-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Avoidant (anxious) personality disorders</li>
<li>Patients are persistently anxious and show great sensitivity to criticism or rejection by others which may lead to social withdrawal. They show great desire for companionship and are generally shy.</li>
<li>They display a pattern of social inhibition, feelings of inadequacy and hypersensitivity to negative evaluation.</li>
</ul>
<p>This situation begins by early adulthood and present in a variety of contexts:</p>
<ul>
<li>Avoids occupational activities that involve significant interpersonal contact, because of fears of criticism, disapproval or rejection.</li>
<li>Is unwilling to get involved with people unless certain of being liked.</li>
<li>Show restraint with intimate relationships because of fear of being shamed or ridiculed.</li>
<li>Is preoccupied with being criticized or rejected in social situations.</li>
<li>Is inhibited in new interpersonal situations because of feelings of inadequacy.</li>
<li>Views self as socially inept, personally unappealing, or inferior to others.</li>
<li>Is usually reluctant to take personal risks or to engage in any new activities because they may prove to be embarrassing.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dependent-personality-disorders">Dependent personality disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dependent-personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This disorder is characterized by pervasive patterns of dependent and submissive behaviour related to an excessive need to be taken care of. The patients are indecisive, lack initiative and avoid responsibility. They fear being alone and usually seek others on whom they can depend. They are often pessimistic, passive and cannot express aggressive feelings. They cling to others for fear of abandonment and often persevere maltreatments for long periods.</p>
<p>They are at increased risk of depression especially associated with the loss of the person they are dependent on. Very common in females. Characterized by the following symptoms:</p>
<ul>
<li>Has difficulty making everyday decisions without excessive amount of advice and reassurance from others.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Need others to assume responsibility for most major areas of his or her life.</p>
<p>Has difficulty expressing disagreement with others because of fear of loss of support or approval.</p>
<p>Has difficulty initiating projects or doing things on his or her own because of lack self confidence in judgement or abilities rather than a lack of motivation or energy.</p>
<p>Goes to excessive lengths to obtain nurturance and support from others, to the point of volunteering to do things that are unpleasant.</p>
<p>Feels uncomfortable or helpless when alone because of exaggerated fears of being unable to care for himself or herself.</p>
<p>Urgently seeks another relationship as a source of care and support when a close relationship ends.</p>
<p>Is unrealistically preoccupied with fears of being left to take care of himself or herself.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sexual-disorders">SEXUAL DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is persistent impairment of the normal patterns of sexual interest or response. In other words, these are disorders characterized by individuals' failure to respond normally in key areas of sexual functioning, making it difficult to enjoy sexual intercourse.</p>
<ul>
<li>Classification</li>
<li>Gender identity disorders</li>
<li>Psychological and behavioural disorders associated with sexual development and maturation.</li>
<li>Disorders of sexual preference.</li>
<li>Sexual dysfunctions.</li>
<li>Gender identity disorders</li>
</ul>
<p>In these disorders, the sense of one's masculinity or femininity is disturbed. They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Transsexualism</li>
</ul>
<p>In this there is persistent and significant sense of discomfort regarding one anatomic sex, and a feeling that it is inappropriate to one's perceived gender. The person will be preoccupied with the wish to get rid of the one's genitals and secondary sex characteristics and to adopt the sex characteristics of the other sex.</p>
<ul>
<li>Management</li>
<li>Counseling to help the individual reconcile with the anatomic sex.</li>
<li>Sex change to the desired gender (sex reassignment surgery) in some selected cases.</li>
<li>Gender identity disorder of childhood</li>
</ul>
<p>This is a disorder similar to transsexualism, with a very early age of onset.</p>
<ul>
<li>Dual role transvetism</li>
</ul>
<p>It is characterized by wearing clothes of the opposite sex in order to enjoy the temporary experience of membership of the opposite sex but without any desire for permanent sex change.</p>
<ul>
<li>Intersexuality</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient has gross anatomical or physiological features of the other sex. For example pseudo hermaphroditism, turnerssyndrome, congenital adrenal hyperplasia.</p>
<ul>
<li>Psychological and behavioural disorders associated with sexual development and maturation</li>
<li>Homosexuality</li>
</ul>
<p>In this, sexual relationships are maintained between persons of the same sex. Female homosexuals are called as "lesbians" and male homosexuals are called as "gay."</p>
<ul>
<li>Management</li>
<li>Behaviour therapy: aversion therapy, covert sensitization, systematic desensitization.</li>
<li>Supportive psychotherapy</li>
<li>Psychoanalytic therapy.</li>
<li>Disorders of sexual preference or paraphilias</li>
</ul>
<p>In paraphilias sexual arousal occurs persistently and significantly in response to objects, which are not part of normal sexual arousal. These disorders include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fetishism: sexual arousal occurs with non-living object which is usually intimately associated with the human body. The fetish objects may include bras, underpants, shoes, gloves etc.</li>
<li>Transvetism: sexual arousal occurs by wearing clothes of the opposite sex.</li>
<li>Sexual sadism: the person is sexually aroused by physical and psychological humiliation, suffering or injury of the sexual partner.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
S
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Sexual masochism: here the person is sexually aroused by physical or psychological humiliation or injury inflicted on self by others.</p>
<p>Exhibitionism: in this the person is sexually aroused by the exposure of one's genitalia to unsuspecting stranger.</p>
<p>Voyeurism: this is persistent or recurrent tendency to observe unsuspecting persons naked (usually of the other sex) and engaged in the sexual activity.</p>
<p>Frotteurism: this is a persistent or recurrent involvement in the act of touching and rubbing against an unsuspecting, non-consenting person.</p>
<p>Pedophilia: it is characterized by persistent or recurrent involvement of an adult in sexual activity with prepubertal children.</p>
<p>Zoophilia (bestiality): involving in sexual activity with animals.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Behavioural therapy: aversion therapy</p>
<p>Psychoanalysis</p>
<p>Drug therapy: antipsychotics have been used for severe aggression associated with paraphilias.</p>
<p>Sexual dysfunctions</p>
<p>This is a significant disturbance in the sexual response cycle, which is not due to an underlying organic cause.</p>
<p>The common dysfunctions are:</p>
<p>Frigidity: absence of desire for sexual activity.</p>
<p>Impotence: the disorder is characterized by an inability to have or sustain penile erection till the completion of satisfactory sexual activity.</p>
<p>Premature ejaculation: ejaculation before completion of satisfactory sexual activity for both partners.</p>
<p>Non-organic vaginismus: an involuntary spasm of the lower 1/3rd of the vagina, interfering with coitus.</p>
<p>Non-organic dyspareunia: pain in the genital area of either male or female during coitus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Psychoanalysis</p>
<p>Hypnosis</p>
<p>Group psychotherapy</p>
<p>Behaviour therapy</p>
<p>Nursing intervention in a patient with sexual disorder</p>
<p>Assess patient's sexual history and previous level of satisfaction in sexual relationships; also assess patient's perception of the problem.</p>
<p>Note cultural, social, ethnic, racial and religious factors that may contribute to conflicts regarding variant sexual practices.</p>
<p>Assess for medication which might be affecting libido.</p>
<p>Provide information regarding sexuality and sexual functioning, correct any misconceptions if necessary. Teach the patient that sexuality is a normal human response and that it involves complex inter-relationships among one's self-concept, body image, family and cultural influences.</p>
<p>Both the patient and his/her partner may need additional assistance if problems in sexual relationship are severe or remain unresolved.</p>
<p>Refer for additional counseling or sex therapy if required.</p>
<p>Assist the therapist as necessary in plan of behaviour modification to help decrease variant behaviour.</p>
<p>In all cases, an accepting and non-judgemental attitude on the part of the nurse is highly essential for successful resolution of these problems as these are highly sensitive issues and maybe causing significant distress to the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="substance-use-disorders">SUBSTANCE USE DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-use-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definitions">DEFINITIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drug: this refers to any chemical agent that once taken in the body is capable of causing physiological and psychological changes. The term "drug" is interchangeably used with "substance."</p>
<p>Psychoactive substance: this is a chemical compound that produces emotional, cognitive or behavioral changes which may be pleasurable or desirable to the user, with adverse medical consequences and is socially unsanctioned because of its undesirable effects on the user and others.</p>
<p>Use: relative to a licit substance, use refers to a situation where a person takes psychoactive substance with no subsequent harm to health, social and occupational function.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Abuse: is a pathological pattern of use where one experiences loss of control and begins to suffer health, social and occupational effects.</p>
<p>Criteria for substance abuse</p>
<p>A maladaptive pattern of substance use leading to clinically significant impairment or distress, as manifested by one or more of the following, occurring within a 12 month period:</p>
<p>Recurrent substance use resulting in a failure to fulfill major role obligations at work, school, or home (e.g. repeated absences or poor work performance related to substance use; substance related absences, suspensions, or expulsions from school; neglect of children or household.)</p>
<p>Recurrent substance use in situations in which it is physically hazardous (e.g. driving or operating a machine when impaired by substance use)</p>
<p>Recurrent substance related legal problems (e.g. arrests for substance related disorderly conduct)</p>
<p>Continued substance despite having persistent or recurrent social or interpersonal problems caused or exacerbated by the effects of the substance (e.g. arguments with spouse about consequences of intoxication, physical fights)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tolerance">Tolerance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tolerance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The need for more of the drug in order to achieve a similar effect realized before at a lower dose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dependence">Dependence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dependence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Refers to the compulsion to take the drug on a continuous basis in order to feel its effect and to further avoid the discomfort of its absence. Dependence can be both be physical and psychological.</p>
<p>Criteria for dependence</p>
<p>A maladaptive pattern of substance use, leading to clinically significant impairment or distress, as manifested by the following occurring at any time in the same 12-month period:</p>
<p>Tolerance as defined by need for markedly increased amounts of the substance to achieve intoxication or desired effect or markedly diminished effect with continued use of the same amount of the substance.</p>
<p>Withdrawal as manifested by the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>The characteristic withdrawal syndrome for the substance (refer to criteria A and B)</li>
<li>The same (or a closely related) substance is taken to relieve or avoid withdrawal symptoms.</li>
<li>The substance is often taken in larger amounts or over a longer period than was intended.</li>
<li>There is a persistent desire or unsuccessful efforts to cut down or control substance use.</li>
<li>A great deal of time is spent in activities necessary to obtain the substance (e.g. visiting multiple doctors or driving long distances), use the substance (e.g. chain smoking), or recover from its effects.</li>
<li>Important social, occupational, or recreational activities are given up or reduced because of substance use.</li>
<li>The substance use is continued despite knowledge of having persistent or recurrent physical or psychological problem that is likely to have been caused or exacerbated by the substance (e.g. continued drinking despite recognition that an ulcer was made worse by alcohol consumption)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="substance-intoxication">Substance intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological changes that are due to the effect of the substance on the central nervous system (e.g. belligerence (aggressive), mood labiality, cognitive impairment, impaired judgment, impaired social or occupational functioning) and develop during or shortly after use of the substance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="substance-withdrawal">Substance withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#substance-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The development of a substance specific syndrome due to the cessation or (or reduction in) substance use that has been heavy and prolonged.</p>
<p>The substance specific syndrome causes clinically significant distress or impairment in social occupational or other important areas of functioning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="commonly-abused-substances">Commonly abused substances<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#commonly-abused-substances" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Alcohol, cocaine, opioids.</li>
<li>Amphetamines, hallucinogens</li>
<li>Cannabis, nicotine, sedatives</li>
<li>Etiological factors in alcohol and substance abuse</li>
<li>Involves an interaction of three main factors: the agent; host and environment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="agent-alcohol-and-other-substances">AGENT (ALCOHOL AND OTHER SUBSTANCES)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#agent-alcohol-and-other-substances" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These substances have a euphoric and calming effect. This is why they are repeatedly used, eventually leading to development of tolerance, withdrawal from prolonged use of a substance, manifests in a syndrome which is characterized</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>65</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>by physical and psychological discomfort. One therefore avoids this uncomfortable state by taking the substance on a continuous basis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="host-individual">HOST(INDIVIDUAL)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#host-individual" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Individuals who are prone to alcohol and substance abuse have some inherent predisposing factors. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Genetic factors: dependence on alcohol has a degree of genetic predisposition. An individual is likely to be alcoholic if the parents or siblings are.</li>
<li>Family drug use: children often accept and copy the behaviour of their elders when they grow up and this may include alcohol and substance abuse.</li>
<li>Peer pressure: in order to belong to certain social groupings and conforming to the norms of the group, pressure within the group may result in an individual member acquiring habits that are maladaptive such as these.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mental-state">Mental state<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-state" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This refers to the emotional attitude regarding the use of a substance and can be negative, positive or neutral. A negative attitude subsequent to influence of religion, social, political or family beliefs will lead to rejection of the substance. A positive attitude will be one that encourages use of the substance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environmental-factors">Environmental factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In environments where supply and availability of the substance is widespread, susceptible individuals may begin to use the substance. Other factors that enhance substance use and abuse are poverty, unemployment, dysfunctional families, migration and rapid urbanization.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="alcohol">ALCOHOL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the most widely abused substance in the world over. It is also the drug that gives the most serious health and social effects in the societies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects">Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="physiological-effects">Physiological effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiological-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="1-alcohol-intoxication">1) Alcohol intoxication:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-alcohol-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>This is seen after recent ingestion of alcohol. There is a clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological change (e.g. inappropriate sexual or aggressive behaviour, mood labiality, impaired judgement, impaired social or occupational functioning)</p>
<p>One or more of the following signs develop during or shortly after alcohol use:</p>
<ul>
<li>Slurred speech, Inco-ordination, unsteady gait, nystagmus, impairement in attention or memory, stupor or coma.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other body effects include: cutaneous vasodilation, increased salivation and gastric salivation, increased output of adrenal steroids and suppression of the antidiuretic hormone leading to diuresis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="chronic-effects">Chronic effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Following chronic use, alcohol is capable of causing damage to all body systems. The amount of damage will depend on amounts taken, duration of drinking.</p>
<p>Digestive system: predisposes to multiple oral problems, esophagitis, cancer of the oesophagus, gastric ulcers, liver cirrhosis and pancreatitis.</p>
<p>CVS: predisposes to high blood pressure and alcoholic cardiomyopathy.</p>
<p>Reproductive system: leads to loss of libido, erectile dysfunction and consequent infertility. For pregnant mothers who consume large amounts the baby may suffer from general growth retardation, low intelligence and congenital abnormalities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="psychological-effects">Psychological effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychological-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These result from direct toxic effect, withdrawal or nutritional deficiencies. Immediate effects are pathological intoxication and alcoholic blackout. Withdrawal gives rise to two forms of withdrawal states (with or without delirium)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="withdrawal-state-withdrawal-syndrome">Withdrawal state (withdrawal syndrome)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#withdrawal-state-withdrawal-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This happens when there is stoppage or reduction in alcohol use that has been heavy and prolonged. Two or more of the following developing within several hours to a few days after stopping or reducing the amount:</p>
<ul>
<li>Autonomic hyperactivity (e.g. sweating or pulse rate greater than 100)</li>
<li>Increased hand tremor</li>
<li>Insomnia</li>
<li>Nausea or vomiting</li>
<li>Transient visual, tactile, or auditory hallucinations or illusions.</li>
<li>Psychomotor agitation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Anxiety</p>
<p>Grand mal seizures.</p>
<p>Withdrawal state with delirium</p>
<p>It is a more serious condition and usually manifests 3 to 4 days after the total cessation or reduction in usual amounts of alcohol taken.</p>
<p>The commonest form of withdrawal is delirium tremens. DT is self-limiting and short lived, but could be fatal.</p>
<p>Initially the clinical picture resembles that of withdrawal state without delirium, but as the condition progresses the person becomes delirious and confused.</p>
<p>Clinical features include prodromal symptoms of insomnia, anxiety, fear, restlessness, tremors and convulsions. As the condition progresses there is clouding of consciousness, disorientation and profound confusion.</p>
<p>The condition tends to get worse at night.</p>
<p>Long-term effects</p>
<p>Nutritional deficiencies lead to Wernicke’s encephalopathy, korsakoff’s psychosis and alcoholic dementia</p>
<p>Social effects</p>
<p>Alcohol use and abuse leads to dysfunctional social and occupational functions at individual, family, community and national level.</p>
<p>At individual level: there is common problem of personality deterioration. Such people lack a sense of responsibility. In economic terms, there is general reduction in income. Student suffers poor academic performance.</p>
<p>At family level: domestic violence is common occurrence and usually results in dysfunctional families, separation and divorce. Children from such families develop serious emotional disorders, usually leading to poor academic performance.</p>
<p>At the community level: associated with high crime rates and indiscipline.</p>
<p>At the national level: the burden of caring for the substance dependent individual is enormous. Such persons contribute to loss of many hours through absenteeism, repeated treatments for depression and physical ailments.</p>
<p>Diagnosis for alcohol use problems</p>
<p>CAGE is a common simple and effective screening tool. The following questions are asked:</p>
<p>Have you ever tried to cut down your drinking? (C)</p>
<p>Do you get annoyed when people talk about your drinking? (A)</p>
<p>Do you ever feel guilty about your drinking? (G)</p>
<p>Do you ever take an early morning drinking? (E)</p>
<p>Other screening tools include:</p>
<p>Alcohol use disorders identification tests (AUDIT)</p>
<p>Short Michigan alcohol screening test (S-MART)</p>
<p>Laboratory investigations or markers:</p>
<p>Blood alcohol concentration (BAC)</p>
<p>Breathe alcohol levels</p>
<p>CANNABIS SATIVA (BHANG)</p>
<p>This is a green flowering plant that is widely grown in the tropical regions in Africa.</p>
<p>Other common names include: marijuana, hashish, njaga, ganja, kikoola, kipapi and dagga.</p>
<p>Commonly forms of use</p>
<p>Dry leaves are usually smoked alone or mixed with ordinary tobacco. The fresh leaves are boiled in water and taken with tea. The same leaves can also be chewed or eaten fresh.</p>
<p>Features of its intoxication</p>
<p>A. Recent use of cannabis.</p>
<p>B. clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological changes (e.g. impaired motor coordination, euphoria, anxiety, sensation of slowed time, impaired judgement, social withdrawal) that developed during, or shortly after, cannabis use.</p>
<p>C. Two or more of the following signs developing within two hours of cannabis use:</p>
<p>Conjunctivainjection, increased appetite, dry mouth, tachycardia.</p>
<p>Health effects</p>
<p>Mild sedation and stimulation.</p>
<p>Feeling of relaxation and well-being.</p>

<p>A slowed sense of time.</p>
<p>Increased appetite.</p>

<p>Chronic and heavy use can lead to lung diseases including cancers, immune suppression, a motivation syndrome and interference with male reproductive functions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="catha-edulis-khat">CATHA EDULIS (KHAT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#catha-edulis-khat" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a crop that is indigenous to Eastern Africa and Yemen. It is also known as Miraa, mairungi and khat. Once taken, khat produces euphoria, suppresses appetite and hunger, and makes one alert.</p>
<p>Thus it is used for relaxation, to facilitate communication at social events and to suppress sleep and fatigue in work situations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-forms-of-use">Common forms of use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-forms-of-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The leaves are chewed fresh, sometimes together with chewing gum or soft drinks. Other users combine khat with alcohol and other substances of abuse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-effects">Health effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Khat produces dependence, tolerance and withdrawal symptoms.</p>
<p>Oral-dental complications, gastritis and constipation.</p>
<p>In men spermatorrhoea and erectile dysfunction.</p>
<p>Some individuals experience psychosis with prominent paranoia and hallucinations.</p>
<p>However khat a crop of significant economic value in many countries. It therefore remains a legal substance.</p>
<p>The clinical features of khat are similar to those of amphetamines, thus intoxication and withdrawal can be summarized using information on amphetamines.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="amphetamine-intoxication">AMPHETAMINE INTOXICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amphetamine-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. recent use of amphetamine or a related substance (e.g. methylphenidate)</p>
<p>B. clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological changes (e.g. euphoria or affective blunting; changes in sociability; hyper vigilance; interpersonal sensitivity; anxiety; tension or anger, stereotyped behaviours, impaired judgement; or impaired social or occupational functioning) that developed during, or shortly after use of amphetamine or a related substance.</p>
<p>Two or more of the following, developing during, or shortly after use of amphetamine or a related substance:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tachycardia or bradycardia</li>
<li>Pupillary dilatation.</li>
<li>Elevated or lowered pressure</li>
<li>Perspiration or chills.</li>
<li>Nausea or vomiting.</li>
<li>Evidence of weight loss.</li>
<li>Psychomotor agitation or retardation.</li>
<li>Muscular weakness, respiratory depression, chest pain, or cardiac arrhythmias.</li>
<li>Confusion, seizures, dyskesis, dystonias, coma.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="amphetamine-withdrawal">Amphetamine withdrawal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amphetamine-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dysphoric mood and two or more of the following physiological changes, developing within a few hours to several days after cessation:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fatigue, vivid unpleasant dreams, insomnia or hyper insomnia, increased appetite, psychomotor retardation or agitation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="heroin-opiates">HEROIN (OPIATES)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heroin-opiates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Opium is a coagulated juice from the unripe capsule of a flowering plant called papaver somniferum.</p>
<p>Other common names for heroin include boy, white lady, brown sugar, junk and muggo. Morphine and codeine are key medicinal products of the plant. From morphine, heroine can be illegally produced by a simple chemical process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-forms-of-use">Common forms of use<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-forms-of-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Consumption is mainly through smoking of the drug mixed with either tobacco or marijuana, sniffed or snorted from foil that is heated from underneath. Can be injected into the veins.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="opioid-intoxication">Opioid intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opioid-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. recent use of an opioid.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>B. clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological changes (e.g. initial euphoria followed by apathy, dysphoria, psychomotor agitation or retardation, impaired judgement, or impaired social or occupational functioning) that developed during or shortly after opioid use.</p>
<p>Pupillary constriction (or pupillary dilatation due to anoxia from severe overdose) and one or more of the following sign, developing during, or shortly after, opioid use:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drowsiness or coma.</li>
<li>Slurred speech.</li>
<li>Impairment of attention or memory.</li>
</ul>
<p>Health effects</p>
<ul>
<li>Development of dependence is high with the use of heroin</li>
<li>The user experiences an intense pleasurable feeling ('rush or euphoria')</li>
<li>There is a degree of analgesia and drowsiness</li>
<li>The eyes are red and the pupil constricted.</li>
<li>Others may experience nausea, cough suppression or depressed respiration.</li>
<li>In the long term, there is damage to the nasal septum, respiratory infections and constipation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Opioid withdrawal</p>
<p>Three or more of the following developing within several minutes to several days after criteria A:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dysphoric mood, nausea and vomiting, muscle aches, lacrimation or rhinorrhea, pupillary dilatation, piloercetion, or sweating, diarrhea, yawning, fever, insomnia.</li>
</ul>
<p>COCAINE</p>
<p>This is a white powder that is extracted from the leaves of the coca bush (erythroxylon coca)</p>
<p>Common street names include: snow, lady, bazooka, crude, flun and snow dust.</p>
<p>Coca is mainly grown in South America.</p>
<p>Common form of use</p>
<p>Use is mainly by snorting or smoking. It can be smoked either directly or mixed with tobacco and also injected SC or IV.</p>
<p>HEALTH EFFECTS</p>
<p>After taking cocaine the user experiences a feeling of physical and mental wellbeing.</p>
<p>There is increased alertness and energy.</p>
<p>Hunger is suppressed and there is significant reduction of fatigue with resultant malnutrition.</p>
<p>The pupils dilate with an increase in heart rate, body temperature and blood pressure.</p>
<p>With larger doses, hallucinations, talkativeness and hyper-excitability may ensue.</p>
<p>High doses can also lead to convulsions or stroke from cerebral hemorrhage.</p>
<p>Cocaine intoxication</p>
<p>A. Recent use of cocaine</p>
<p>B. clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological changes (e.g. euphoria or affective blunting, changes in sociability; hyper vigilance; interpersonal sensitivity; anxiety, tension, or anger, stereotyped behaviours, impaired judgement or impaired social or occupational functioning) that developed during, or shortly after use of cocaine.</p>
<p>Two or more of the following, developing during, or shortly after, cocaine use:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tachycardia or bradycardia.</li>
<li>Pupillary dilation.</li>
<li>Elevated or lowered blood pressure.</li>
<li>Perspirations or chills.</li>
<li>Nausea or vomiting.</li>
<li>Evidence of weight loss.</li>
<li>Psychomotor agitation or retardation.</li>
<li>Muscular weakness, respiratory depression, chest pain, or cardiac arrhythmias</li>
<li>Confusion, seizures, dyskinesia, dystonias or coma.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cocaine withdrawal</p>
<p>A. dysphoric mood and two or more of the following physiological changes, developing within a few hours to several days after.</p>
<p>Fatigue, vivid unpleasant dreams, insomnia or hypersomnia, increased appetite, psychomotor retardation or agitation.</p>
<p>SOLVENTS</p>

<p>Also called inhalants, this group represents the many chemicals that are inhaled to get high. They include varnish, petrol, glue, aerosols, nail polish remover and cleaning detergents.</p>
<p>Since many are domestic or industrial chemicals, they are easily obtained.</p>
<p>Abuse is by sniffing from a piece of cloth that is socked with the chemical. Others directly inhale the chemical from a container or plastic bag.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inhalant-intoxication">Inhalant intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inhalant-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. recent use</p>
<p>B. clinically significant maladaptive behavioural or psychological changes (e.g. belligerence, assaultiveness, apathy, impaired judgement, impaired social or occupational functioning) that developed during or shortly after use of or exposure to volatile inhalants.</p>
<p>Two or more of the following signs developing during or shortly after inhalant use or exposure:</p>
<p>Dizziness, nystagmus, Inco-ordination, slurred speech, unsteady gait, lethargy, depressed reflexes, psychomotor retardation, tremor, generalized muscle weakness, blurred vision or diplopia, stupor or coma, euphoria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nicotine-withdrawal">NICOTINE WITHDRAWAL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nicotine-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Daily use of nicotine for at least several weeks.</p>
<p>B. abrupt cessation of nicotine use, or reduction in the amount of nicotine used, followed within 24 hours by four or more of the following signs:</p>
<p>Dysphoric or depressed mood, insomnia, irritability, frustration, or anger, anxiety, difficulty concentrating, restlessness, decreased heartrate, increased appetite or weight gain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-management">PRINCIPLES OF MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Substance use or dependence is a treatable disease.</p>
<p>Management of substance related disorder aims at assisting individuals to attain reasonable state of function and involves taking the patient through a multi-disciplinary programme.</p>
<p>The management process involves detoxification, rehabilitation, relapse prevention, after-care, social and vocational rehabilitation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="detoxification">Detoxification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#detoxification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the first stage in treatment and is the process of helping the individual to stop using the substance without experiencing painful effects.</p>
<p>Detoxification, which usually lasts 3-7 days, can be medical or psychological and the setting maybe in or outpatient.</p>
<p>In medical detoxification, medication similar to what was being used by the client is given:</p>
<p>Alcohol-chlordiazepoxide:</p>
<p>Cannabis-Haloperidol</p>
<p>Cocaine-Ritalin</p>
<p>Heroin-Methadone</p>
<p>If the substitute medication is not available, symptomatic relief of the presenting symptoms in combination with psychological support is recommended.</p>
<p>Psychological treatments target behavioural, social and psychological triggers that continued substance use. They are used to motivate the client to stop using substances and to improve interpersonal functioning.</p>
<p>During such treatments, clients are taught life skills and how to deal with family problems and pressure from friends who use substances. They are also taught relapse prevention techniques by increasing involvement in substance free social, vocational and family activities. Clients are encouraged to make lifestyle changes and address problems resulting from years of dependence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rehabilitation">Rehabilitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rehabilitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This focuses on full recovery, which involves preparing the client for social re-intergration. It further involves helping the client in skill development and job training. Where possible, employment opportunities are also extended to the client.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relapse-prevention">Relapse prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relapse-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a process of not starting substance use again through counseling. The process of relapse follows a predictable pattern. Signs of impending relapse can be identified by the therapist and the patient. There are warning signs in behaviour and thinking that patients can be taught to monitor. They need to learn the indicators of stress and anxiety such as insomnia, nervousness or headaches, and to view these as signals of possible relapse. Once the relapse indicators are</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>identified, a plan to intervene needs to be quickly enacted. Learning from previous relapse is critical. The relapse starts with triggers. Triggers are people, places, objects, feelings and times which cause people cravings.</p>
<p>After care</p>
<p>The aftercare programme ensures the client follows up treatment and also serves to review the client’s status. This is achieved through effective participation in self-help or support groups.</p>
